# PRD

1. Overview
Objective:
Develop a lightweight, AI-powered 8-bit ghost widget that resides on the user’s desktop. The ghost dynamically changes color, expressions, and mood in response to user interactions (e.g., mouse movements) and system events, and it leverages basic AI functionality for conversational and adaptive behavior.

Target Platform:

Desktop environments: Windows, Mac, and Linux

Easy installation/uninstallation with a small footprint

Key Differentiators:

Charming Animations & Varied Expressions: A richly animated ghost with a spectrum of moods (idle, happy, playful, tired) that reacts in real time.

Dynamic AI Interactions: Optional AI connectivity to provide conversational responses and deeper mood adaptation.

Seamless Desktop Integration: The widget stays on top of other windows and integrates naturally with desktop activity.

2. User Stories
Idle Ghost:
As a user, I want to see a calm, neutral 8-bit ghost in a grayscale idle state when I’m not interacting with it, ensuring it remains unobtrusive.

Happy Color Change:
As a user, I want the ghost to shift to a brighter, lively color palette (e.g., pastel or neon) when I move my mouse rapidly or hover over it, signaling engagement.

Curious Mouse Reaction:
As a user, I want the ghost to animate (e.g., tilt its head, pop an exclamation mark) when my cursor is near, providing a playful, interactive experience.

Emotion Cycles:
As a user, I want the ghost to display varied moods (excited, sleepy, playful) triggered by time-based events or patterns in my activity, keeping the experience fresh.

AI-Enhanced Interaction:
As a user, I want the ghost to offer conversational responses or context-aware suggestions through integrated AI, making the experience more interactive and personalized.

Easy Customization:
As a user, I want the ability to rename the ghost, adjust animation speeds, and customize the color schemes for specific moods.

3. Features & Functionality
3.1 Core Ghost States
Idle:

Gentle floating animation in grayscale when no significant interaction is detected.

Happy:

Vibrant, colorful mode activated on mouse hover or increased desktop activity.

Playful/Surprised:

Quick “pop” or tilt animation when the cursor moves rapidly nearby.

Tired/Sleepy:

Droopy eyes or slow animation triggered after a period of inactivity.

3.2 Animation & Expression Library
Facial Expressions:

Animated eyes (blinking, squinting, looking left/right) and subtle mouth changes.

Body Movements:

Bouncing, swaying, or quick spins to enhance interactivity.

Optional Accessories:

Occasional appearance of a ghostly hat or themed accessory for events (e.g., birthdays, holidays).

3.3 Dynamic Reactions
Mouse Interaction:

Continuously track cursor proximity to trigger localized animations (e.g., ghost “following” or “shying away”).

Inactivity Timeout:

Automatically transition to a “tired” state after a predefined idle period.

Special Triggers:

Double-click on the ghost opens a settings panel for customization (rename, color schemes, etc.).

3.4 AI Connectivity (Optional, Future Scope)
Conversational Engagement:

Integration with a lightweight AI or chatbot API to allow simple textual or voice-based interactions.

Mood Adaptation:

AI-driven insights to adjust the ghost’s mood based on contextual user data and usage patterns.

3.5 User Customization Options
Personalization:

Allow users to rename the ghost.

Customizable color palettes for different moods.

Animation Controls:

Adjustable animation speed and intensity settings.

4. Design & Art Style
Pixel Art Aesthetic:

Adhere to a classic 8-bit design with clearly defined pixels and a limited color palette.

Default state in grayscale; color variety emerges during interactions (happy state, special moods).

Visual Transitions:

Smooth, frame-based animations ensuring transitions between moods feel natural.

Consistent art style across all ghost animations and accessories.

UI/UX Considerations:

Ensure that the ghost remains visually appealing without being intrusive.

Maintain clarity and ease of interaction even in smaller widget sizes.

5. Technical Architecture
5.1 Core Engine
Development Framework:

Primary option: Electron (JS/HTML/CSS) for cross-platform compatibility.

Alternative: Native desktop frameworks (e.g., C++/Qt) if performance demands increase.

Animation Techniques:

Utilize sprite sheets or frame-based animations for smooth transitions.

Leverage CSS animations for simple state changes where applicable.

5.2 Event Listeners & Interaction Handling
Mouse Movement Detection:

Capture and calculate cursor coordinates relative to the ghost’s position.

User Inactivity:

Implement timers to detect periods of inactivity and trigger the “tired” state.

AI Input Processing:

Process simple text or voice inputs (if enabled) to generate context-aware responses.

5.3 State Management
Finite State Machine (FSM):

Model the ghost’s behavior with defined states: Idle → Happy → Playful/Surprised → Tired → Idle.

Transitions managed by user interaction events and time-based triggers.

5.4 Integration & Deployment
Installation & Startup:

Easy one-click installation packages.

Option to launch on system startup with a toggle in the settings.

Resource Efficiency:

Ensure low CPU/GPU usage to avoid performance degradation on the host system.

6. Risks & Considerations
Performance Optimization:

Continuous polling (e.g., mouse tracking) must be optimized to prevent excessive resource usage.

Cross-Platform Variability:

OS-specific constraints may affect window transparency, always-on-top behavior, and widget interactions.

Privacy Concerns:

Clearly communicate data usage policies, especially if AI connectivity involves sending data to external services.

AI Limitations:

Ensure fallback mechanisms if AI connectivity fails or is disabled, maintaining core functionality.

7. Roadmap
MVP (Minimum Viable Product)
Basic 8-bit ghost with grayscale idle animation.

Mouse hover triggers immediate color change and simple animated reactions.

Inactivity timeout triggers a tired/sleepy animation.

Basic settings for renaming and toggling the widget on/off.

Post-MVP Enhancements
Expanded range of mood animations and more sophisticated expression changes.

Integration with a lightweight AI for conversational interactions and contextual mood adaptations.

Seasonal themes and special accessory triggers (e.g., holiday hats).

Advanced customization options for power users (e.g., animation speed, AI behavior adjustments).

8. Success Metrics
User Engagement:

Track frequency and diversity of interactions (state changes, AI conversation usage).

Performance Metrics:

Monitor CPU/GPU usage; ensure minimal impact on system performance.

Adoption & Retention:

Measure download numbers, active usage statistics, and user feedback.

User Satisfaction:

Conduct surveys and feedback sessions to assess enjoyment and usability of the ghost widget.
================================================================================

# BinaryHeart RAG PRD

Below is a Product Requirements Document (PRD) for the Multi-Modal RAG System, consolidating the core requirements, system architecture, feature specifications, and success criteria. This document is intended to guide stakeholders and developers through the entire project scope.

1. Introduction
1.1 Purpose
The purpose of this project is to develop a Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG) system that can:

Ingest and index various file types (text, images, spreadsheets, code) from a local folder or via uploads.
Provide semantic search capabilities.
Generate context-aware responses with citations using Anthropic’s Claude API.
Handle large datasets while maintaining efficient performance and preserving data privacy.
1.2 Objectives
Multi-Modal Input Support: Seamlessly parse text documents, spreadsheets, PDFs, images (with OCR and scene understanding), and code files.
Flexible Retrieval: Provide a robust indexing mechanism that allows semantic search across a diverse corpus.
Contextual Responses: Integrate with Claude’s API to deliver highly accurate, context-rich answers, including links/citations to original file locations.
User-Friendly Interface: Offer a minimalistic yet powerful web interface for uploading files, selecting the RAG folder, and querying the data.
Scalable: Efficiently handle large data volumes (up to 10GB+) and manage smaller context windows for Claude’s API.
2. Scope
2.1 In Scope
A local FastAPI backend service that orchestrates:
Data ingestion (folder scanning, file uploads).
File parsing and content extraction (including OCR and image analysis with Claude).
Semantic indexing and retrieval using LangChain + FAISS.
Query handling and response generation via Claude.
A basic frontend using HTML/Jinja2 templates for uploading files, searching, and displaying responses.
Support for standard file types:
Text: .pdf, .docx, .txt
Spreadsheets: .xlsx, .csv
Images: .png, .jpg, .jpeg (with OCR + scene description)
Code: .py, .js, .java, etc.
2.2 Out of Scope
Authentication or user management (may be added later if needed).
Advanced UI design or complex front-end frameworks (minimal, functional interface is sufficient).
Deployment to cloud or container platforms (initially designed for local Windows environment).
3. System Architecture
mathematica

│ - Semantic Retrieval        │
└─────────────┬──────────────┘
              │
┌─────────────▼──────────────┐
│    Anthropic’s Claude       │
│ - Processes Context & Query │
│ - Generates Responses       │
└─────────────────────────────┘
4. Detailed Requirements
4.1 Data Ingestion
Folder Selection

Users can select a local folder (“RAG Folder”) where bulk files reside.
The system scans the folder recursively, preserving hierarchy (subfolders, file names).
File Uploads

The web interface supports batch uploads of new files.
Newly uploaded files are placed in the RAG folder (or indexed in memory) for immediate parsing.
Organizing & Indexing

Maintain metadata about each file: file name, type, path, last modified date.
Store file hierarchy to preserve folder context (e.g., /Projects/Module1/file.py).
4.2 File Parsing and Preprocessing
Text Documents
DOCX, PDF, TXT: Extract text using python-docx, PyPDF2 or PyMuPDF, and basic file I/O for .txt.
Spreadsheets (XLSX, CSV): Convert each cell to text using openpyxl or CSV readers. Consider multi-sheet support.
Images
OCR
Perform OCR using pytesseract to extract any textual content within the image.
Scene Understanding
Call Claude’s API with the image data or an intermediate representation (as feasible) to retrieve a semantic description:
Objects in the scene, relationships, activities, or contextual notes.
The “purpose” or “key message” of the image if discernible.
Store the returned image description as text in the final document corpus (e.g., “Image Description: ...”).
Metadata
Keep track of image file names, folder structure, and embedded text or descriptions for reference.
Code Files
Support common code extensions (.py, .js, .java, etc.).
The system reads the file contents for indexing.
Optionally parse docstrings, function definitions, or class names to enhance search.
4.3 Indexing
Chunking
Use LangChain to chunk large documents (including code, spreadsheets, and extracted text from images) into smaller, meaningful sections.
Embedding
Generate vector embeddings with either OpenAI Embeddings or Hugging Face models.
Associate each chunk with:
Content (text).
File path or image description.
Additional metadata (folder hierarchy, file type).
Vector Store (FAISS)
Store embeddings in FAISS for efficient nearest-neighbor search.
Maintain metadata to enable quick retrieval of relevant chunks.
4.4 Querying
Search Interface
A simple text box in the web interface to accept user queries.
Semantic Search
Use LangChain’s retrieval pipeline to find the most relevant chunks from the FAISS index.
Combine multiple chunks if they come from different documents.
Context Prompt Construction
Assemble the retrieved chunks into a prompt that is passed to Claude’s API.
Keep track of references for each chunk to later cite the source.
4.5 Response Generation
Claude API Integration
Send the constructed prompt (retrieved text, user query) to Claude.
Manage the context window by limiting the total tokens within Claude’s limit.
Citations & Output
The response is displayed in the UI along with references to the source files.
Example citation format: (Source: /RAG_Folder/SubFolder/filename.pdf, p. 2)
5. Web Interface
5.1 Folder Selector
Allows user to specify the base RAG folder.
Triggers a re-index of the selected folder.
5.2 File Uploader
Supports multiple file uploads at once.
Automatically parses and indexes the newly uploaded content.
5.3 Query Bar
Users type in questions or requests for information.
On submission, the system searches the index and queries Claude.
5.4 Response Display
Shows the response text from Claude.
Displays citations with links or file references.
6. Tech Stack
6.1 Core Components
LangChain for document parsing, chunking, and retrieval orchestration.
FAISS for vector-based similarity search.
Anthropic API (Claude) for conversational AI and image understanding.
6.2 File Handling
PDFs: PyMuPDF or PyPDF2
Word Docs: python-docx
Spreadsheets: openpyxl or CSV parsing
Images: Pillow (for image handling) + pytesseract (for OCR)
Code: Native file reading (with potential advanced parsing if needed)
6.3 Backend
FastAPI: Provides endpoints for file upload, folder selection, search query processing, and integration with Claude.
6.4 Frontend
HTML/Jinja2 templates for basic UI functionality (folder selection, file upload form, query input, response output).
6.5 Additional Tools
Tesseract OCR: Local installation required for text extraction from images.
Hugging Face: Optional advanced embedding models (if not using OpenAI embeddings).
7. Project Deliverables
Functional System:

Local FastAPI service with endpoints for:
Folder-based indexing.
File uploading and parsing.
Query handling and response generation.
Incorporation of image analysis (OCR + Claude’s semantic description).
Context-rich responses that cite relevant files.
Web Interface:

Simple, user-friendly layout:
Folder selector.
File upload mechanism (batch upload).
Query input field.
Results area showing responses and file references.
Scalability:

Capable of handling up to 10GB+ of mixed data.
Uses chunking and retrieval to manage smaller context windows for Claude’s API.
Security and Privacy:

Runs on Windows locally (no cloud-based file storage required).
Potential for optional file/embedding encryption to protect sensitive data.
Documentation:

Setup instructions (installation, environment configuration).
Developer notes on how to extend or maintain the system.
End-user guide describing folder selection, uploading, and search usage.
8. Milestones & Timeline (Example)
Week 1:
Project setup, environment configuration, Tesseract installation, basic FastAPI scaffold.
Week 2:
Implement file ingestion & parsing for text documents and code files.
Integrate LangChain + FAISS for indexing.
Week 3:
Add image parsing with OCR and Claude-based scene descriptions.
Refine chunking and embedding strategies.
Week 4:
Build the query pipeline: search + context assembly + Claude request.
Implement citations and link references in responses.
Week 5:
Develop the front-end (Jinja2 templates).
Perform integration tests with a sample data set.
Week 6:
Performance optimizations (handle large data sets).
Final QA, documentation, and deployment readiness.
9. Risks & Mitigation
Large File Handling:

Risk: Memory usage spikes with very large files (codebases, large PDFs).
Mitigation: Use chunking strategies, stream processing, and careful memory management.
OCR Accuracy:

Risk: Tesseract may produce errors on low-quality images.
Mitigation: Encourage higher-resolution images; possibly integrate additional OCR libraries if needed.
API Rate Limits:

Risk: Anthropics Claude may have usage or rate limitations.
Mitigation: Cache image descriptions and reuse them. Manage call frequency in code.
Context Window Limits:

Risk: Claude’s token limit could truncate large prompts.
Mitigation: Retrieve only the top N relevant chunks and dynamically limit prompt size.
10. Acceptance Criteria
Functional:
The system can successfully parse and index a wide range of file formats.
Users can query the system and receive context-rich responses citing correct file references.
Performance:
Indexing 10GB of data completes without crashes (within reasonable time).
Query responses are generated within a user-acceptable latency (e.g., <10 seconds).
Reliability:
The system handles multiple uploads and queries without data corruption or errors.
Usability:
Non-technical users can navigate the basic UI to upload files, select a folder, and retrieve answers.
================================================================================

# speaking ideas

info about joshes keynote: Signature Keynotes

🔥 Keynote: The Unfair Advantage — What Prison Taught Me About Becoming Great

Most people think prison breaks you. For me, it revealed what was already broken—and forced me to rebuild with truth.

In this powerful keynote, Joshua Sinn shares the raw, life-changing lessons he learned while serving 10 years behind bars. But this isn’t a prison talk. This is a human talk. Because the very things he discovered in confinement—discipline, clarity, accountability, stillness, and inner purpose—are the same principles that drive greatness in life, leadership, and business.

In a world filled with distraction and ego, Joshua makes the case that isolation can be a gift, pain can be a teacher, and pressure can shape you—if you let it.

Whether you’re running a company, rebuilding your life, or just trying to find meaning in the chaos, this keynote is an invitation to look within, awaken your purpose, and tap into your own unfair advantage.

Core Lessons from “The Unfair Advantage”

Stillness births clarity — Prison stripped away the noise. What would happen if we created stillness on purpose?
Discipline is freedom — Without structure, potential dies. Structure saved my life.
Responsibility is power — The moment I stopped blaming, I started building.
Pain can be your greatest teacher— It didn’t break me. It showed me what needed to change.
Purpose is the real exit — The key to freedom was never a door. It was within.

Key Takeaways:

✅ Learn how adversity can awaken clarity, mission, and true identity
✅ Discover the power of stillness in a noisy, distracted world
✅ Understand why responsibility is the doorway to transformation
✅ Unlock a mindset that turns pain into progress and failure into fire
✅ Realize you don’t need to be incarcerated to be stuck—and you don’t need to be free to be powerful

“For some, prison broke them. For me, it gave me purpose. It showed me that if I never give up—I can’t lose.”

💎 Impossible is a Mindset: Rewriting Your Story

💡 Keynote: Impossible Is a Mindset — Discovering Purpose Through Pain

What if your pain wasn’t a setback—but a signal?

In this powerful keynote, Joshua Sinn takes audiences on a transformational journey where pain is no longer the enemy, but the entry point to purpose. Built from his lived experience and the foundation of Impossible the Movement, this talk unveils how impossibility is not a circumstance—it’s a mindset. And just as it’s learned, it can be unlearned.

Joshua introduces 10 powerful principles and 5 core values forged in the fire of adversity—tools that helped him turn a prison cell into a training ground for greatness. These aren't just ideas. They're blueprints for personal and professional breakthrough.

Whether you're overcoming trauma, rebuilding your life, or leading others through uncertainty, this keynote equips you with the mental framework to turn pain into purpose and impossibility into impact.

🔑 The 10 Principles That Unlock Purpose

Integrity – Living aligned with truth, even when no one is watching.
Mindset – Rewiring your thoughts to overcome limits and create new outcomes.
Purpose – Finding the “why” that makes pain worth enduring.
Opportunist – Seeing doors where others see dead ends.
Synergy – Building power through unity and collaboration.
Sacrifice – Giving up what’s comfortable to rise into what’s calling.
Imagination – Envisioning what’s possible before it exists.
Belief – Holding onto faith, even in the dark.
Legacy – Living today in a way that echoes tomorrow.
Equip – Not just rising alone, but lifting others with you.

❤️ The 5 Values That Ground the Movement

Love – The foundation of healing and connection.
Humility – Choosing growth over ego.
Non-Judgment – Seeing beyond someone’s worst moment.
Unity – Recognizing we rise together or not at all.
Service – Turning survival into contribution.

Key Takeaways:

✅ Discover how your pain holds the blueprint to your purpose
✅ Learn the 10 mindset shifts that turn struggle into strategy
✅ Activate the 5 values that create lasting change in self and others
✅ Walk away with a transformational framework you can live, lead, and build with

“Impossible isn’t a condition. It’s a decision. And when you choose purpose over pain, the impossible starts to move.”

Who Joshua Speaks To

✅ Correctional Facilities
✅ Juvenile Detention Centers
✅ Schools & Youth Programs
✅ Faith-Based Organizations
✅ Sober Living & Recovery Centers
✅ Conferences & Corporate Events

“He didn’t just speak to the inmates—he sparked a movement behind bars. He got through to people no one else could.”
— Program Director, CDCR

Meet Joshua Sinn

Founder of Impossible the Movement | Speaker | Transformation Coach

Joshua Sinn spent 10 years in prison—but what looked like the end was only the beginning. It was behind bars that he discovered his purpose, began building his legacy, and sparked a movement that changed lives from the inside out. After his release, Joshua launched Impossible the Movement, helping others turn their pain into purpose. Since then, he’s spoken at prisons, schools, recovery centers, and more—impacting thousands with his raw truth and transformative message.

He’s also built 7 sober livings in 14 months, collaborated on a short film documenting his journey, and continues to deliver messages that awaken and empower.

“Joshua’s voice is the one the world needs right now.”
— Event Organizer, Youth Summit

Let’s Work Together

Whether you're planning a conference, prison program, school assembly, or leadership retreat—Joshua delivers powerful, unforgettable talks that move hearts and minds.

                        <div class="tab-content space-y-4 min-h-[240px]">
                            <!-- His Story Tab -->
                            <div id="story" class="tab-pane active">
                                <p class="text-gray-300">
                                    Joshua Nishida Sinn is a recovery coach, motivational speaker, and advocate for rehabilitation & reentry, who turned a ten-year prison sentence into an unlikely launch pad for a movement to change lives. Behind bars, Josh became a certified recovery coach, designed fitness-based rehabilitation programs, and laid the foundations of Impossible the Movement - now a nonprofit that spans sober living programming, prison wellness initiatives, and a fast-growing network of advocacy partners.
                                </p>
                            </div>
                            
                            <!-- His Speaking Tab -->
                            <div id="work" class="tab-pane hidden">
                                <p class="text-gray-300">
                                    Today, Josh keynotes rehabilitation conferences, correctional facilities, schools, and community events. He speaks about the life-changing lessons he learned in confinement--how stillness breeds clarity, discipline becomes freedom, and pain, framed correctly, can reveal purpose. Drawing from his own journey through addiction, incarceration, and reentry, Joshua delivers raw, practical insights and advice that resonates with those navigating adversity.
                                </p>
                            </div>
                            
                            <!-- His Impact Tab -->
                            <div id="impact" class="tab-pane hidden">
                                <p class="text-gray-300">
                                    Since his release, Josh has developed rehabilitative programs for sober livings and fitness programs for prisons, helping reduce recidivism and promote recovery. His messages are backed by experience, practical, and centered on the idea that stillness creates clarity, discipline leads to freedom, and that purpose is the true path to lasting change.
                                </p>
                                <p class="text-gray-300 mt-4">
                                    Whether he's speaking to incarcerated youth or corporate leaders, Josh equips audiences with the mindset shifts and values that turn pain into purpose and struggle into motivation. He's not just telling a redemption story, he helps others write their own.
                                </p>
                            </div>
                        </div>
                    </div>
                </div>
            </div>
        </section>

    <div id="footer-placeholder"></div>

    <script>
        document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
            // Intersection Observer for fade-in elements
            const fadeInObserver = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {
                entries.forEach(entry => {
                    if (entry.isIntersecting) {
                        entry.target.classList.add('visible');
                    }
                });
            }, { threshold: 0.1 });
            
            // Observe all fade-in elements
            document.querySelectorAll('.fade-in').forEach(el => {
                fadeInObserver.observe(el);
            });
            
            // Observe keynote cards with delay
            const keynoteCards = document.querySelectorAll('.keynote-card');
            keynoteCards.forEach((card, index) => {
                setTimeout(() => {
                    fadeInObserver.observe(card);
                }, index * 150); // Staggered delay
            });
            
            // Parallax effect for background
            window.addEventListener('scroll', function() {
                const scrolled = window.scrollY;
                const parallaxBg = document.getElementById('parallax-bg');
                
                if (parallaxBg) {
                    parallaxBg.style.transform = 'translateY(' + (scrolled * 0.4) + 'px)';
                }
            });
            
            // Hide scroll button when scrolled past hero section
            window.addEventListener('scroll', function() {
                const scrollButton = document.querySelector('.scroll-button');
                const heroHeight = document.querySelector('section').offsetHeight;
                
                if (window.scrollY > heroHeight * 0.8) {
                    scrollButton.style.opacity = '0';
                } else {
                    scrollButton.style.opacity = '1';
                }
            });

            // Load header and footer from base.html
            fetch('base.html')
                .then(response => {
                    if (!response.ok) {
                        throw new Error(`HTTP error! status: ${response.status}`);
                    }
                    return response.text();
                })
                .then(html => {
                    const parser = new DOMParser();
                    const doc = parser.parseFromString(html, 'text/html');
                    
                    const headerContent = doc.querySelector('header');
                    if (headerContent) {
                        const headerPlaceholder = document.getElementById('header-placeholder');
                        if (headerPlaceholder) {
                            headerPlaceholder.replaceWith(headerContent);
                        } else {
                            console.error('Header placeholder not found in speaking.html');
                        }
                    } else {
                        console.error('Header element not found in base.html content.');
                    }
                    
                    const footerContent = doc.querySelector('footer');
                    if (footerContent) {
                        const footerPlaceholder = document.getElementById('footer-placeholder');
                        if (footerPlaceholder) {
                            footerPlaceholder.replaceWith(footerContent);
                        } else {
                            console.error('Footer placeholder not found in speaking.html');
                        }
                    } else {
                        console.error('Footer element not found in base.html content.');
                    }

                    // Re-initialize scripts that depend on header/footer content
                    if (window.MobileMenu && typeof window.MobileMenu.setupBehavior === 'function') {
                        window.MobileMenu.setupBehavior();
                    }
                    initializeHeaderScroll();
                })
                .catch(error => {
                    console.error('Error fetching or parsing base.html:', error);
                });

            function initializeHeaderScroll() {
                const nav = document.querySelector('header nav'); 
                if (nav) {
                    const initialNavClasses = Array.from(nav.classList);
                    let isTransparent = initialNavClasses.includes('bg-transparent');

                    window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
                        if (window.scrollY > 50) {
                            if (isTransparent) {
                                nav.classList.remove('bg-transparent');
                                nav.classList.add('bg-gray-900/60');
                                isTransparent = false;
                            }
                        } else {
                            if (!isTransparent) {
                                nav.classList.remove('bg-gray-900/60');
                                nav.classList.add('bg-transparent');
                                isTransparent = true;
                            }
                        }
                    }, { passive: true });
                } else {
                    // console.warn('Nav element not found for scroll effect after header injection.');
                }
            }

            // Tab functionality
            const tabBtns = document.querySelectorAll('.tab-btn');
            const tabPanes = document.querySelectorAll('.tab-pane');
            
            tabBtns.forEach(btn => {
                btn.addEventListener('click', function() {
                    // Remove active class from all buttons and hide all panes
                    tabBtns.forEach(b => b.classList.remove('active', 'text-blue-300', 'border-b-2', 'border-blue-300'));
                    tabBtns.forEach(b => b.classList.add('text-gray-400'));
                    tabPanes.forEach(p => p.classList.add('hidden'));
                    tabPanes.forEach(p => p.classList.remove('active'));
                    
                    // Add active class to clicked button and show corresponding pane
                    this.classList.add('active', 'text-blue-300', 'border-b-2', 'border-blue-300');
                    this.classList.remove('text-gray-400');
                    
                    const tabId = this.getAttribute('data-tab');
                    const activePane = document.getElementById(tabId);
                    activePane.classList.remove('hidden');
                    activePane.classList.add('active');
                });
            });
        });
        
        // Scroll to next section function
        function scrollToNextSection() {
            const heroSection = document.querySelector('section');
            const nextSection = heroSection.nextElementSibling.nextElementSibling;
            
            if (nextSection) {
                nextSection.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
            }
        }
    </script>
</body>
</html>

    <script>
        // Load header and footer from base.html
        fetch('base.html')
            .then(response => {
                if (!response.ok) {
                    throw new Error(`HTTP error! status: ${response.status}`);
                }
                return response.text();
            })
            .then(html => {
                const parser = new DOMParser();
                const doc = parser.parseFromString(html, 'text/html');
                
                const headerContent = doc.querySelector('header');
                if (headerContent) {
                    const headerPlaceholder = document.getElementById('header-placeholder');
                    if (headerPlaceholder) {
                        headerPlaceholder.replaceWith(headerContent);
                    } else {
                        console.error('Header placeholder not found in partner_with_us.html');
                }
                } else {
                    console.error('Header element not found in base.html content.');
                }
                
                const footerContent = doc.querySelector('footer');
                if (footerContent) {
                    const footerPlaceholder = document.getElementById('footer-placeholder');
                    if (footerPlaceholder) {
                        footerPlaceholder.replaceWith(footerContent);
                    } else {
                        console.error('Footer placeholder not found in partner_with_us.html');
                    }
                } else {
                    console.error('Footer element not found in base.html content.');
                }

                // Re-initialize scripts that depend on header/footer content
                if (window.MobileMenu && typeof window.MobileMenu.setupBehavior === 'function') {
                    window.MobileMenu.setupBehavior();
                }
                initializeHeaderScroll();
            })
            .catch(error => {
                console.error('Error fetching or parsing base.html:', error);
            });

        function initializeHeaderScroll() {
            const nav = document.querySelector('header nav'); 
            if (nav) {
                const initialNavClasses = Array.from(nav.classList);
                let isTransparent = initialNavClasses.includes('bg-transparent');

                window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
                    if (window.scrollY > 50) {
                        if (isTransparent) {
                            nav.classList.remove('bg-transparent');
                            nav.classList.add('bg-gray-900/60');
                            isTransparent = false;
                        }
            } else {
                        if (!isTransparent) {
                            nav.classList.remove('bg-gray-900/60');
                            nav.classList.add('bg-transparent');
                            isTransparent = true;
                        }
                    }
                }, { passive: true });
            } else {
                // console.warn('Nav element not found for scroll effect after header injection.');
            }
        }
    </script>
</body>
</html>

# PRD

1. Overview
Product Name: Macro Recorder & Replayer
Description: A cross-platform desktop application written in C++ that records all user keystrokes and mouse actions, then replays them on-demand with adjustable speed and repetition settings.

2. Objectives & Goals
High Performance & Accuracy
Use C++’s native speed to handle large, high-frequency input recordings without slowdowns.
Easy Recording & Playback
Provide a simple workflow to record and replay keystrokes/mouse actions across different applications.
Flexible Playback Options
Allow speed adjustments, custom delays, and repeated loops during playback.
Macros Management
Store, edit, rename, and organize multiple recorded “macro” files.
Cross-Platform Support
Target Windows, macOS, and Linux using a unified C++ codebase (e.g., with Qt or similar).
3. Scope
In-Scope

Recording keyboard and mouse actions, including movement, clicks, scroll, special keys (shortcuts).
Saving and loading macros to a local data format (JSON, binary, etc.).
Editing event sequences (inserting/removing events, reordering).
A minimal but user-friendly GUI (likely built with Qt or similar).
Out-of-Scope

Conditional logic (if/else flows).
Automated UI element detection or on-screen image recognition.
High-level security features (encryption, advanced permissions).
4. Functional Requirements
4.1 Recording
Trigger & Stop

A Record button in the UI.
Application minimizes or goes to system tray during recording.
A global hotkey (e.g., Shift+Alt+F12) stops recording so user doesn’t have to restore the UI.
Captured Events

Keyboard: Key press/release, including combinations (Ctrl + C, etc.).
Mouse: Movement (x,y), clicks (left, right, middle), wheel scroll events.
Timestamp: Each event has a high-resolution timestamp relative to the start of recording.
Data Storage

Use either:
Binary serialization for speed/efficiency (e.g., Protocol Buffers, FlatBuffers, or custom).
JSON if readability and debugging are priorities.
Save the data upon stopping the recording.
4.2 Playback
Initiation

User selects an existing macro or the freshly recorded one from the UI.
A Play button triggers playback; optionally provide a global hotkey as well.
Timing & Speed

Default: replay intervals as recorded (1:1 timing).
Option: set a multiplier (e.g., 2× faster or 0.5× slower).
Option: insert extra fixed delays (e.g., +50ms each event).
Repetition

User can specify the number of times the macro should loop (finite or infinite).
Playback can be stopped via a button or global hotkey.
4.3 Editing & Management
Macro Editing

A basic interface (table/list) showing each event’s timestamp, type (mouse/keyboard), and relevant details.
Users can remove or reorder events; optionally insert new events or delays.
Macro Management

Display a list of saved macros (by name or ID).
Options to rename, delete, or load macros for editing or playback.
5. Non-functional Requirements
Implementation

C++ for the core logic, hooking, and event simulation.
A cross-platform framework like Qt for the GUI (alternatively, wxWidgets or Dear ImGui).
Cross-Platform

Must run on Windows, macOS, and Linux.
Use OS-specific hooks/APIs under a unified interface.
Windows: Low-level hooks via SetWindowsHookEx (WH_KEYBOARD_LL / WH_MOUSE_LL).
macOS: I/O Kit or Quartz Event Taps.
Linux: X11 or Wayland event capture (depending on environment).
Performance

Buffer events in memory during recording to avoid excessive disk I/O.
Minimize overhead by capturing raw data efficiently (e.g., ring buffer or vector).
Ensure real-time replay with minimal drift.
Reliability & Stability

Handle partial recordings gracefully (e.g., if the app exits unexpectedly).
Provide clear error handling if hooking fails (permissions, etc.).
Usability

Clear indicators for when the app is recording (icon or tray message).
Simple, intuitive GUI for start/stop and basic macro management.
Privacy & Security

Data is only stored locally.
No external data transmission or advanced encryption required (personal use).
6. User Flows
Recording Flow

Launch the app; the UI shows an empty or existing macro list.
Click Record → App confirms recording and minimizes.
Perform keyboard/mouse actions in any application.
Press global hotkey (Shift+Alt+F12) to stop.
App window pops up, prompting for a macro name and storage location.
Playback Flow

User selects a recorded macro from the list.
Adjust speed multiplier and repetition count (if desired).
Click Play → App replays all events in the chosen speed and loop.
Stop playback via hotkey or UI button.
Editing Flow

User selects a macro → clicks Edit.
App displays a table of events with timestamps and details.
User removes, reorders, or changes timing.
Saves the modified macro (new or overwrite existing).
7. Technical Considerations
Global Hooks

On Windows, implement a DLL-based SetWindowsHookEx for system-wide hooking (WH_KEYBOARD_LL/WH_MOUSE_LL).
On macOS, use Quartz Event Taps. Ensure proper permissions are set in “Accessibility.”
On Linux, handle X11 or Wayland events. This may require separate code paths if you want to support both.
Event Buffering

Use an in-memory structure like std::vector<Event> to store data.
Write to file after the user stops recording to avoid real-time disk overhead.
Threading

A dedicated thread for capturing/queueing events to avoid blocking the main UI thread.
Another thread for asynchronous file I/O when saving the macro data (optional).
Timestamp Management

Record high-resolution timestamps (e.g., std::chrono::high_resolution_clock) to preserve precise intervals.
Convert intervals to real-time or scaled delays during playback.
Playback Simulation

For keyboard events, simulate press/release at the OS level.
For mouse, move the pointer to recorded coordinates and replicate click/scroll.
Insert user-defined delays or multiply recorded intervals by a speed factor.
GUI Framework

Qt recommended for consistent cross-platform UIs.
Build a minimal application window with record/play/edit functions.
8. Future Enhancements (Not in MVP)
Conditional Logic: e.g., “if a window changes, do X.”
UI Element Detection: Wait for a specific button or coordinate color before proceeding.
Encryption: Secure macros containing sensitive data.
Cloud Sync: Option to store macros remotely for multi-device usage.
9. Success Criteria
High Performance: Large, fast streams of events (e.g., many mouse move events per second) don’t cause lag or data loss.
Accuracy: Playback reproduces recorded actions with minimal deviation.
Stability: App handles unexpected closures or hooking issues gracefully.
Ease of Use: Straightforward to record, save, and replay macros in the user’s daily workflow.
Cross-Platform Reliability: The same codebase compiles and runs effectively on Windows, macOS, and Linux.
================================================================================

# Idea

I'll provide detailed instructions for an AI developer to create your Roku City-inspired driving experience:
Roku City Driving Experience - Developer Instructions
Concept Overview
Create a 3D driving experience inspired by Roku City (the screensaver environment from Roku devices) where:

The user is permanently inside a car traveling along a predefined path
The car automatically drives through the cityscape
Users can look around 360° but cannot control the car's movement or exit the vehicle
The experience follows a scenic route along futuristic buildings, waterfront areas, and other iconic Roku City elements

Key Visual Elements from Roku City

Futuristic, slightly retro-futuristic architecture with neon accents
Tall skyscrapers with distinct shapes and illuminated windows
Art deco and cyberpunk aesthetic influences
Vibrant color palette dominated by blues, purples, and neon highlights
Water elements reflecting city lights
Animated billboards and signs
Constant nighttime/dusk setting with dramatic lighting

Technical Requirements

Three.js Implementation

Use Three.js for 3D rendering
Implement an optimized rendering pipeline for smooth performance
Support for postprocessing effects (bloom, ambient occlusion)

Camera System

First-person perspective from inside the car
Mouse/touch controls for looking around
Optional: VR support for immersive experience

Vehicle & Path System

Create a spline-based path system for the car to follow
Implement smooth camera movement along the path
Add slight camera bobbing/physics for realism
Gradual acceleration/deceleration at path segments

Environment

Section 1: Downtown skyscrapers area
Section 2: Waterfront boulevard with reflections
Section 3: Entertainment district with theaters and billboards
Section 4: Residential towers and parks
Looping path that connects all areas seamlessly

Lighting & Atmosphere

Dynamic lighting with neon signs and street lamps
Bloom effect for neon elements
Fog effect for depth and atmosphere
Reflection and refraction for water surfaces

Performance Optimization

LOD (Level of Detail) for buildings
Instancing for repeated elements
Occlusion culling for non-visible objects
Texture atlasing for efficient GPU usage

User Experience Considerations

Smooth, relaxing journey with gentle turns
Varied scenery to maintain interest
Ambient audio with city sounds and relaxing music
Optional time-of-day cycle
Optional weather effects (rain, for added reflections)

Implementation Approach

Create the base environment and path system
Add core buildings and terrain
Implement the car and camera controls
Add lighting and basic materials
Enhance with detailed models and textures
Implement postprocessing effects
Add audio and atmosphere
Optimize for performance

# Security

Security Assessment Report for sendi.fi
Overall Security Score: 6.5/10
Critical Vulnerabilities
Password Storage (CRITICAL)
Passwords are stored in plaintext in the users Map and subsequently in data/users.json
Fix: Implement password hashing using bcrypt or Argon2 with proper salt
Impact: High - Could lead to complete account compromise if data is breached
Session Management (HIGH)
No session expiration mechanism implemented
Sessions are stored in memory and persist indefinitely
Fix: Implement session timeouts and proper session invalidation
Impact: Medium - Could lead to unauthorized access through session hijacking
Security Concerns
File Upload Security
Large file size limit (25GB) could enable DOS attacks
No file type validation or scanning
Recommendations:
Implement virus scanning
Add file type validation
Consider reducing maximum file size
Implement rate limiting
Data Storage
Sensitive data stored in plain JSON files
No encryption at rest
Fix: Use a proper database with encryption at rest
Impact: Medium - Local file access could expose all data
Authentication
No password complexity requirements
No rate limiting on login attempts
No MFA support
Fix: Implement all of the above security measures
Positive Security Measures
NGINX Configuration
Strong SSL/TLS configuration (TLS 1.2 and 1.3 only)
Good security headers implemented:
X-Frame-Options
X-XSS-Protection
X-Content-Type-Options
Content-Security-Policy
HSTS
Proper access controls for sensitive directories
Input Validation
Some basic input validation present
File upload size limits implemented
Secure file naming implementation
CORS Configuration
Production environment restricts to sendi.fi domain
Specific allowed methods and headers
Detailed Recommendations
Authentication & Authorization
Apply
Session Management
Apply
File Upload Security
Apply
Rate Limiting
Apply
Additional Security Recommendations
Implement Database
Replace file-based storage with a proper database (e.g., PostgreSQL)
Enable encryption at rest
Implement proper backup procedures
Logging and Monitoring
Implement structured logging
Add error tracking
Set up security event monitoring
Implement audit logs for sensitive operations
API Security
Add API rate limiting
Implement request validation
Add API versioning
Consider implementing API keys for different clients
Infrastructure Security
Regular security updates
Implement backup procedures
Set up monitoring and alerting
Configure proper firewall rules
Security Score Breakdown
Authentication & Authorization: 5/10
Session Management: 6/10
Data Storage: 5/10
File Upload Security: 7/10
NGINX Configuration: 9/10
Input Validation: 7/10
Error Handling: 7/10
Logging & Monitoring: 6/10
Overall Score: 6.5/10
The system has some good security measures in place, particularly in the NGINX configuration and basic input validation. However, there are several critical issues that need to be addressed, particularly around password storage and session management. The implementation of the recommended fixes would significantly improve the security posture of the application.

# Chat.tsx

import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import { styles } from './styles';
import { API_BASE, getTimeRemaining, ChatMessage } from './types';
import { mobileStyles } from './mobileStyles';
import { isMobileDevice } from './utils';

interface ChatProps {
  sessionId: string;
  handleLogout: () => void;
}

export function Chat({ sessionId, handleLogout }: ChatProps) {
  const [messageInput, setMessageInput] = useState('');
  const [messages, setMessages] = useState<ChatMessage[]>([]);
  const [isLoading, setIsLoading] = useState(false);
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);
  const [expandedMessages, setExpandedMessages] = useState<Set<string>>(new Set());
  
  const isMobile = isMobileDevice();

  const handleSendMessage = async () => {
    if (!messageInput.trim() || !sessionId) return;
    
    setIsLoading(true);
    try {
      console.log('Sending message:', {
        url: `${API_BASE}/messages`,
        content: messageInput,
        sessionId: sessionId
      });
      
      const res = await fetch(`${API_BASE}/messages`, {
        method: 'POST',
        headers: {
          'Content-Type': 'application/json',
          'sessionid': sessionId
        },
        body: JSON.stringify({ content: messageInput }),
        credentials: 'include'
      });
      
      console.log('Message response:', {
        status: res.status,
        statusText: res.statusText,
        ok: res.ok
      });
      
      if (!res.ok) {
        const errorBody = await res.text();
        console.error('Error response body:', errorBody);
        throw new Error(`Failed to send message: ${res.status} ${res.statusText}`);
      }
      
      setMessageInput('');
      await fetchMessages();
    } catch (err: any) {
      console.error('Send message error:', err);
      setError(err.message);
    } finally {
      setIsLoading(false);
    }
  };

  const fetchMessages = async () => {
    if (!sessionId) return;
    
    try {
      const res = await fetch(`${API_BASE}/messages`, {
        headers: {
          'sessionid': sessionId
        },
        credentials: 'include'
      });
      
      if (!res.ok) {
        throw new Error('Failed to fetch messages');
      }
      
      const data = await res.json();
      const now = Date.now();
      const activeMessages = data.filter((msg: ChatMessage) => msg.expiresAt > now);
      setMessages(activeMessages);
    } catch (err: any) {
      setError(err.message);
      if (err.message.includes('Unauthorized')) {
        handleLogout();
      }
    }
  };

  useEffect(() => {
    if (sessionId) {
      fetchMessages();
      
      const interval = setInterval(() => {
        fetchMessages();
      }, 10000); // Poll every 10 seconds
      
      return () => clearInterval(interval);
    }
  }, [sessionId]);

  const toggleMessageExpansion = (messageId: string) => {
    if (isMobile) return;
    setExpandedMessages(prevExpanded => {
      const newExpanded = new Set(prevExpanded);
      if (newExpanded.has(messageId)) {
        newExpanded.delete(messageId);
      } else {
        newExpanded.add(messageId);
      }
      return newExpanded;
    });
  };

  return (
    <div style={isMobile ? { ...styles.card, ...mobileStyles.mobileCard, paddingTop: 0 } : styles.card} className="mobile-card">
      {!isMobile && <h2 style={styles.title}>Chat</h2>}
      <div style={{ display: 'flex', flexDirection: 'column', flex: 1, overflow: 'hidden', height: '100%' }}>
        {isMobile && messages.length > 0 && (
          <div style={{ padding: '10px 0', borderBottom: '1px solid #eee', marginBottom: '10px', flexShrink: 0 }}>
            <button
              style={{
                ...mobileStyles.mobileButton,
                width: '100%',
                display: 'flex',
                alignItems: 'center',
                justifyContent: 'center',
                gap: '8px',
                fontSize: '14px',
                padding: '10px'
              }}
              onClick={() => {
                const text = messages
                  .sort((a, b) => a.createdAt - b.createdAt)
                  .map(m => m.content)
                  .join('\n\n');
                navigator.clipboard.writeText(text);
                alert('All messages copied!');
              }}
            >
              <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
                <path d="M8 5H6C4.89543 5 4 5.89543 4 7V19C4 20.1046 4.89543 21 6 21H16C17.1046 21 18 20.1046 18 19V17" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                <path d="M20 9H10C8.89543 9 8 8.10457 8 7V3C8 1.89543 8.89543 1 10 1H16L20 5V7C20 8.10457 19.1046 9 18 9Z" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
              </svg>
              Copy All
            </button>
          </div>
        )}
        <div style={{
          flex: 1,
          overflowY: 'auto',
          padding: isMobile ? '0 8px' : '0 10px',
          marginBottom: '10px',
        }}>
          {messages.length === 0 ? (
            <div style={isMobile ? mobileStyles.mobileEmptyState : styles.emptyState}>
              <svg width="48" height="48" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" style={{ margin: '0 auto 16px' }}>
                <path d="M4 12H20" stroke="#999" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                <path d="M4 4H20" stroke="#999" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                <path d="M4 20H20" stroke="#999" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
              </svg>
              <p style={{ 
                fontSize: '16px', 
                fontWeight: '500', 
                color: '#333', 
                marginBottom: '8px' 
              }}>No messages yet</p>
              <p style={{ 
                fontSize: '14px', 
                color: '#666' 
              }}>Send a message to see it here</p>
            </div>
          ) : (
            <div>
              {!isMobile && (
                 <div style={{ display: 'flex', justifyContent: 'flex-end', marginBottom: '16px' }}>
                  <button
                    style={{ ...styles.secondaryButton, display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', gap: '8px' }}
                    onClick={() => {
                      const text = messages
                        .sort((a, b) => a.createdAt - b.createdAt)
                        .map(m => m.content)
                        .join('\n\n');
                      navigator.clipboard.writeText(text);
                      alert('All messages copied!');
                    }}
                  >
                     <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
                       <path d="M8 5H6C4.89543 5 4 5.89543 4 7V19C4 20.1046 4.89543 21 6 21H16C17.1046 21 18 20.1046 18 19V17" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                       <path d="M20 9H10C8.89543 9 8 8.10457 8 7V3C8 1.89543 8.89543 1 10 1H16L20 5V7C20 8.10457 19.1046 9 18 9Z" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                     </svg>
                    Copy All
                  </button>
                </div>
              )}
              
              {messages
                .sort((a, b) => b.createdAt - a.createdAt)
                .map((message) => (
                  <div
                    key={message.id}
                    style={ isMobile ? 
                      { // Mobile Styles
                        padding: '10px 8px',
                        marginBottom: '8px',
                        backgroundColor: '#f9f9f9',
                        borderRadius: '8px',
                        border: '1px solid #eee',
                        display: 'flex',
                        alignItems: 'flex-start', 
                        gap: '8px',
                      } : 
                      { // Desktop Styles (reference styles.ts)
                         ...styles.fileItem, 
                         marginBottom: '12px', 
                      }
                    }
                    className={isMobile ? "mobile-chat-item" : ""} 
                  >
                    <div style={{ flex: 1, overflow: 'hidden' }}>
                      <pre 
                        style={{
                          whiteSpace: 'pre-wrap', 
                          wordBreak: 'break-word', 
                          margin: 0,
                          fontFamily: 'inherit',
                          fontSize: '14px', 
                          ...(!isMobile ? styles.messageContent : {}),
                          ...(!isMobile && expandedMessages.has(message.id) ? styles.messageContentExpanded : {})
                        }}
                        onClick={() => !isMobile && toggleMessageExpansion(message.id)}
                      >
                        {message.content}
                        {!isMobile && !expandedMessages.has(message.id) && message.content.length > 150 && (
                          <div style={styles.expandMessageIndicator}>Click to expand</div>
                        )}
                      </pre>
                      <div style={{ fontSize: '11px', color: '#666', marginTop: '4px' }}>
                        {getTimeRemaining(message.expiresAt)}
                      </div>
                    </div>
                    
                    <div style={{
                      display: 'flex', 
                      flexDirection: isMobile ? 'column' : 'row', 
                      gap: isMobile ? '6px' : '8px', 
                      alignItems: isMobile ? 'flex-end' : 'center'
                    }}>
                      <button
                         style={{
                            background: 'none',
                            border: 'none',
                            cursor: 'pointer',
                            color: '#666',
                            padding: isMobile ? '2px' : '4px',
                            display: 'flex',
                            alignItems: 'center'
                          }}
                          onClick={() => {
                            navigator.clipboard.writeText(message.content);
                            alert('Message copied!');
                          }}
                      >
                        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
                           <path d="M8 5H6C4.89543 5 4 5.89543 4 7V19C4 20.1046 4.89543 21 6 21H16C17.1046 21 18 20.1046 18 19V17" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                           <path d="M20 9H10C8.89543 9 8 8.10457 8 7V3C8 1.89543 8.89543 1 10 1H16L20 5V7C20 8.10457 19.1046 9 18 9Z" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                        </svg>
                         {!isMobile && <span style={{ marginLeft: '4px', fontSize: '14px' }}>Copy</span>}
                      </button>
                      <button
                         style={{
                            background: 'none',
                            border: 'none',
                            cursor: 'pointer',
                            color: '#e53935',
                            padding: isMobile ? '2px' : '4px',
                            display: 'flex',
                            alignItems: 'center'
                          }}
                          onClick={async () => {
                            if (window.confirm('Delete this message?')) {
                              try {
                                const response = await fetch(`${API_BASE}/messages/${message.id}`, {
                                  method: 'DELETE',
                                  headers: {
                                    'sessionid': sessionId
                                  },
                                  credentials: 'include'
                                });
                                
                                if (!response.ok) {
                                  throw new Error(`Failed to delete message: ${response.status}`);
                                }
                                
                                setMessages(messages.filter(m => m.id !== message.id));
                              } catch (error) {
                                console.error('Error deleting message:', error);
                                alert(error.message || 'Failed to delete message');
                              }
                            }
                          }}
                      >
                        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
                           <path d="M4 7H20" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                           <path d="M10 11V17" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                           <path d="M14 11V17" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                           <path d="M5 7L6 19C6 20.1046 6.89543 21 8 21H16C17.1046 21 18 20.1046 18 19L19 7" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                           <path d="M9 7V4C9 3.44772 9.44772 3 10 3H14C14.5523 3 15 3.44772 15 4V7" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                        </svg>
                         {!isMobile && <span style={{ marginLeft: '4px', fontSize: '14px' }}>Delete</span>}
                      </button>
                    </div>
                  </div>
                ))}
            </div>
          )}
        </div>
        
        <div style={{
          display: 'flex',
          gap: '12px',
          padding: isMobile ? '10px 8px' : '0 10px 10px 10px',
          marginTop: 'auto',
          flexShrink: 0,
        }} className="mobile-actions">
          <textarea
            style={{
              ...styles.input,
              resize: 'none',
              height: isMobile ? '60px' : '80px',
              flex: 1,
              minHeight: '40px',
            }}
            className="mobile-input"
            placeholder="Type your message here..."
            value={messageInput}
            onChange={(e) => setMessageInput(e.target.value)}
            onKeyDown={(e) => {
              if (e.key === 'Enter' && (e.metaKey || e.ctrlKey)) {
                e.preventDefault();
                handleSendMessage();
              }
            }}
          />
          <button
            style={{
              ...styles.button,
              minWidth: isMobile ? '60px' : '100px',
              height: 'auto',
              alignSelf: 'flex-end',
              padding: isMobile ? '10px 14px' : styles.button.padding,
            }}
            className="mobile-button"
            onClick={handleSendMessage}
            disabled={isLoading || !messageInput.trim()}
          >
            Send
          </button>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

# chatmobile.tsx

import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import { styles } from './styles'; // Keep styles for fallback/shared styles if needed
import { API_BASE, getTimeRemaining, ChatMessage } from './types';
import { mobileStyles } from './mobileStyles';
import { isMobileDevice } from './utils'; // Keep this for consistency, though logic is mobile-only now

interface ChatProps {
  sessionId: string;
  handleLogout: () => void;
}

export function ChatMobile({ sessionId, handleLogout }: ChatProps) {
  const [messageInput, setMessageInput] = useState('');
  const [messages, setMessages] = useState<ChatMessage[]>([]);
  const [isLoading, setIsLoading] = useState(false);
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);
  // No expandedMessages state needed for mobile

  const handleSendMessage = async () => {
    if (!messageInput.trim() || !sessionId) return;
    
    setIsLoading(true);
    try {
      console.log('Sending message:', {
        url: `${API_BASE}/messages`,
        content: messageInput,
        sessionId: sessionId
      });
      
      const res = await fetch(`${API_BASE}/messages`, {
        method: 'POST',
        headers: {
          'Content-Type': 'application/json',
          'sessionid': sessionId
        },
        body: JSON.stringify({ content: messageInput }),
        credentials: 'include'
      });
      
      console.log('Message response:', {
        status: res.status,
        statusText: res.statusText,
        ok: res.ok
      });
      
      if (!res.ok) {
        const errorBody = await res.text();
        console.error('Error response body:', errorBody);
        throw new Error(`Failed to send message: ${res.status} ${res.statusText}`);
      }
      
      setMessageInput('');
      await fetchMessages();
    } catch (err: any) {
      console.error('Send message error:', err);
      setError(err.message);
    } finally {
      setIsLoading(false);
    }
  };

  const fetchMessages = async () => {
    if (!sessionId) return;
    
    try {
      const res = await fetch(`${API_BASE}/messages`, {
        headers: {
          'sessionid': sessionId
        },
        credentials: 'include'
      });
      
      if (!res.ok) {
        throw new Error('Failed to fetch messages');
      }
      
      const data = await res.json();
      const now = Date.now();
      const activeMessages = data.filter((msg: ChatMessage) => msg.expiresAt > now);
      setMessages(activeMessages);
    } catch (err: any) {
      setError(err.message);
      if (err.message.includes('Unauthorized')) {
        handleLogout();
      }
    }
  };

  useEffect(() => {
    if (sessionId) {
      fetchMessages();
      
      const interval = setInterval(() => {
        fetchMessages();
      }, 10000); // Poll every 10 seconds
      
      return () => clearInterval(interval);
    }
  }, [sessionId]);

  // No toggleMessageExpansion needed for mobile

  return (
    <div style={mobileStyles.mobileCard} className="mobile-card">
      <div style={mobileStyles.mobileContent}>
        {messages.length > 0 && (
          <div style={{ padding: '10px 16px', borderBottom: '1px solid #eee', marginBottom: '10px', flexShrink: 0 }}>
            <button
              style={mobileStyles.mobileCopyAllButton}
              onClick={() => {
                const text = messages
                  .sort((a, b) => a.createdAt - b.createdAt)
                  .map(m => m.content)
                  .join('\n\n');
                navigator.clipboard.writeText(text);
                alert('All messages copied!');
              }}
            >
              <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
                <path d="M8 5H6C4.89543 5 4 5.89543 4 7V19C4 20.1046 4.89543 21 6 21H16C17.1046 21 18 20.1046 18 19V17" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                <path d="M20 9H10C8.89543 9 8 8.10457 8 7V3C8 1.89543 8.89543 1 10 1H16L20 5V7C20 8.10457 19.1046 9 18 9Z" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
              </svg>
              Copy All
            </button>
          </div>
        )}
        <div style={mobileStyles.mobileMessageList}>
          {messages.length === 0 ? (
            <div style={mobileStyles.mobileEmptyState}>
              <svg width="48" height="48" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" style={{ margin: '0 auto 16px', opacity: 0.7 }}>
                <path d="M4 12H20" stroke="#999" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                <path d="M4 4H20" stroke="#999" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                <path d="M4 20H20" stroke="#999" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
              </svg>
              <p style={{ 
                fontSize: '17px', 
                fontWeight: '500', 
                color: '#333', 
                marginBottom: '8px' 
              }}>No messages yet</p>
              <p style={{ 
                fontSize: '15px', 
                color: '#666' 
              }}>Send a message to see it here</p>
            </div>
          ) : (
            <div>
              {messages
                .sort((a, b) => b.createdAt - a.createdAt)
                .map((message) => (
                  <div
                    key={message.id}
                    style={mobileStyles.mobileChatItem}
                    className="mobile-chat-item"
                  >
                    <div style={{ flex: 1, overflow: 'hidden' }}>
                      <pre 
                        style={{ 
                          whiteSpace: 'pre-wrap', 
                          wordBreak: 'break-word', 
                          margin: 0,
                          fontFamily: 'inherit',
                          fontSize: '15px', 
                        }}
                      >
                        {message.content}
                      </pre>
                      <div style={{ fontSize: '12px', color: '#888', marginTop: '6px' }}>
                        {getTimeRemaining(message.expiresAt)}
                      </div>
                    </div>
                    
                    <div style={{ 
                      display: 'flex',
                      gap: '4px',
                    }}>
                      <button
                        style={mobileStyles.mobileActionButton}
                        onClick={() => {
                          navigator.clipboard.writeText(message.content);
                          alert('Message copied!');
                        }}
                      >
                        <svg width="18" height="18" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
                          <path d="M8 5H6C4.89543 5 4 5.89543 4 7V19C4 20.1046 4.89543 21 6 21H16C17.1046 21 18 20.1046 18 19V17" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                          <path d="M20 9H10C8.89543 9 8 8.10457 8 7V3C8 1.89543 8.89543 1 10 1H16L20 5V7C20 8.10457 19.1046 9 18 9Z" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                        </svg>
                      </button>
                      <button
                        style={mobileStyles.mobileActionButton}
                        onClick={() => {
                          const url = `${API_BASE}/messages/${message.id}`;
                          fetch(url, {
                            method: 'DELETE',
                            headers: {
                              'sessionid': sessionId
                            },
                            credentials: 'include'
                          }).then(() => {
                            fetchMessages();
                          });
                        }}
                      >
                        <svg width="18" height="18" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
                          <path d="M19 7L18.1327 19.1425C18.0579 20.1891 17.187 21 16.1378 21H7.86224C6.81296 21 5.94208 20.1891 5.86732 19.1425L5 7M10 11V17M14 11V17M15 7V4C15 3.44772 14.5523 3 14 3H10C9.44772 3 9 3.44772 9 4V7M4 7H20" stroke="currentColor" strokeWidth="1.5" strokeLinecap="round" strokeLinejoin="round"/>
                        </svg>
                      </button>
                    </div>
                  </div>
                ))}
            </div>
          )}
        </div>
        
        <div style={mobileStyles.mobileMessageContainer}>
          <input
            type="text"
            placeholder="Type your message here..."
            value={messageInput}
            onChange={(e) => setMessageInput(e.target.value)}
            onKeyDown={(e) => {
              if (e.key === 'Enter' && !e.shiftKey) {
                e.preventDefault();
                handleSendMessage();
              }
            }}
            style={mobileStyles.mobileMessageInput}
          />
          <button
            onClick={handleSendMessage}
            disabled={isLoading || !messageInput.trim()}
            style={mobileStyles.mobileSendButton}
          >
            Send
          </button>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
