# PRD

1. Product Overview
Purpose:

The product’s main function is to embed an invisible, highly robust watermark into images (especially AI-generated) and extract it on demand.
The watermark’s goal is to reliably identify AI-generated images, even under adversarial conditions (e.g., cropping, compression).
Key Objectives:

Robustness: The watermark must withstand image transformations such as resizing, compression, cropping, noise injection, and other malicious attempts at removal.
Invisibility: The watermark must be imperceptible to the naked eye.
Usability: A simple web UI that allows users to embed or extract the watermark with minimal steps.
2. Scope and Features
2.1 Core Features
Watermark Embedding

Method: Hybrid spectral watermarking using DWT, SVD, and a chaotic map.
Supported Formats: JPG, PNG, and WEBP.
Performance: Embedding must complete within 1 minute for images up to 10MB.
User Interaction: Single-click embed. No advanced settings exposed in the UI.
Watermark Extraction

Method: Reverse application of chaotic map, SVD, DWT to extract the hidden watermark.
Accuracy: Must reliably detect the watermark despite common image manipulations.
User Interaction: Single-click extraction.
Metadata and Logging

Storage: The application logs watermark embed events (e.g., timestamp, user ID, or basic identifier). No large image data stored on the server; watermarked images go back to the user’s environment.
Security: Minimal user data to ensure privacy while retaining the ability to audit.
2.2 Non-Functional Requirements
Robustness

Must maintain watermark integrity under typical modifications: resizing, compression, minor cropping, noise injection.
Must tolerate moderate malicious attacks aimed at destroying the watermark.
Performance

Each watermark embed or extract operation must finish within 60 seconds for images up to 10MB.
Security

Automated key generation for chaotic map operations and encryption keys.
Must protect the watermark’s cryptographic elements to prevent unauthorized removals.
Scalability

Initially targeted for an MVP, handling typical user traffic without extreme concurrency.
Should allow potential future scaling, but no explicit large-scale concurrency is required at launch.
Usability

Simple, intuitive, minimal user interface.
Single-click “Embed Watermark” and “Extract Watermark” buttons, with no advanced parameters required from the user.
3. Technical Considerations
3.1 Architecture and Stack
Application Type: Web-based.
Server-Side: Flexible — could be implemented in Python (Flask/Django), Node.js, or any robust framework that supports scientific/mathematical processing.
Libraries:
For image processing: OpenCV, Pillow, or equivalent.
For DWT, SVD, and chaotic maps: Libraries or custom implementations that handle 2D DWT, matrix decompositions, and logistic or Arnold’s cat map.
Encryption/Key Management:
Automatically generate and manage keys per session or per embed operation.
Securely store or discard keys based on product strategy (likely minimal storage).
3.2 Algorithm Workflow
Embed

Perform DWT on the original image to a suitable level (e.g., 1-level or 2-level).
Apply SVD to the sub-band where the watermark is to be hidden.
Use a chaotic map (e.g., Logistic or Arnold’s Cat) to scramble the watermark data.
Merge the scrambled watermark data back into the singular values.
Reconstruct the image via inverse SVD and inverse DWT.
Extract

Perform the same DWT on the watermarked image.
Apply SVD on the same sub-band used for embedding.
Use the chaotic map keys to descramble extracted data.
Compare/Verify the extracted watermark signal against expected watermark patterns.
4. User Interface & User Flows
Landing Page

Upload Image button.
On selection, system proceeds to embed or extract based on user choice.
Embedding Flow

Embed Watermark button triggers background server-side processes.
Result: Downloadable watermarked image.
Log: Timestamp and minimal embedding success details.
Extraction Flow

Extract Watermark button triggers background server-side processes.
Result: Visual or textual confirmation that a watermark was found (and details if needed).
Confirmation

Clear messaging: “Watermark successfully embedded” or “Watermark successfully extracted.”
5. Storage, Logging, & Data Management
Local/Session-based Handling

The user’s image is processed in memory or in temporary storage.
After the process completes, the final watermarked image is returned to the user, and the temporary data is cleared.
Log Data

Record basic event data (user ID if applicable, timestamp, success/failure, partial key info if needed for debugging).
No Persistent Image Storage

All watermarked images remain with the user.
Retain no large files on the server beyond the immediate session.
6. Testing & Validation
Functional Tests

Embedding: Confirm watermark is embedded without visible artifacts.
Extraction: Confirm watermark can be extracted accurately under normal usage.
Robustness Tests

Subject watermarked images to typical transformations (crop, rotate, compress) and attempt extraction.
Evaluate success rates and measure bit error rates.
Performance Tests

Ensure typical operations complete under 1 minute for images up to 10MB.
Security Tests

Verify that keys are not exposed.
Confirm that unauthorized users cannot extract or remove watermarks without valid keys.
7. Roadmap & Future Enhancements
Batch Processing

Allow multiple images to be watermarked or verified simultaneously.
Advanced Parameter Settings

Expose toggles for watermark strength, DWT levels, etc. (for advanced users).
Integration with AI Image Generators

Provide an API endpoint for direct embedding in AI output pipelines.
Enhanced Attack-Resistant Methods

Explore further wavelet transforms (e.g., Curvelet or Contourlet) or multi-level chaotic maps for even greater security.
8. Timeline
MVP Phase (2-3 Months)

Implement basic DWT/SVD/chaotic embedding and extraction.
Set up minimal web UI with single-click embed/extract.
Ensure performance for up to 10MB images within 1 minute.
Beta Release (Next 2-4 Weeks)

Conduct robustness testing against common transformations.
Collect user feedback.
Official Launch

Refine performance and security.
Finalize logs and analytics.
9. Success Metrics
Extraction Accuracy

Watermark detection rate under normal and slightly modified images should be near 100%.
User Satisfaction

Fast, reliable watermark embedding and extraction.
Intuitive user experience.
Performance

Embedding/extraction under 1 minute for images up to 10MB.
Summary
This PRD describes a web-based system that uses DWT + SVD + Chaotic Map to embed a robust, invisible watermark into AI-generated images. The focus is on high resilience to adversarial edits, quick processing, and an easy, single-click UI. With strong logging of embed events and minimal server storage, the platform aims to provide a secure, efficient solution to help identify AI-generated images and mitigate disinformation

# PRD BHAI Assistant

Product Requirements Document (PRD)

Project: BinaryHeart AI Assistant
Ultimate Goal of the Project
To develop a chat-based AI assistant that supports BinaryHeart's mission by enhancing organizational efficiency, creativity, and decision-making. The assistant will provide strategic suggestions, automate repetitive workflows, summarize documents, and facilitate idea generation aligned with BinaryHeart's goals.

Ultimate Goal of the User
To interact seamlessly with an intelligent assistant that provides actionable insights, organizes tasks, and generates innovative ideas tailored to BinaryHeart's specific data and goals. The AI should simplify work processes and be intuitive for BinaryHeart team members to use.

Functional Scope and Features
Core Features

Chat-based Query Handling: Enable users to interact with the assistant for real-time suggestions, ideas, and solutions.
Document Summarization: Generate concise summaries from uploaded documents.
Strategic Suggestions: Provide targeted recommendations for fundraising, partnerships, sustainability, and chapter scaling.
Task Prioritization: Assist in managing tasks and resource allocation across BinaryHeart's chapters.
Idea Generation: Continuously brainstorm ideas and respond to queries with creative solutions.
Multimedia Analysis: Analyze charts, images, and other multimedia for actionable insights.
Underlying Technology

Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG): Combine dynamic retrieval from the repository with generative capabilities for precise and context-aware outputs.
Multimedia Analysis Library: Use AI models capable of processing visual and textual data simultaneously.
Repository Management: Allow team members to update and structure data, ensuring AI responses are current and relevant.
Access and Deployment

Dedicated App Interface: Mobile- and web-friendly platforms.
User Roles: Restrict access to BinaryHeart team members.
Scalability: Ensure seamless integration of new chapters, data, and features.
Development Phases
Phase 1: Planning and Architecture
Define Architecture

AI Engine: Choose GPT-like models fine-tuned with BinaryHeart’s data.
Repository Management: Organize data into folders with metadata tags for efficient retrieval.
App Interface: Design a simple, intuitive chat interface.
Key Questions to Address

How will multimedia data (charts, PDFs, etc.) be analyzed?
What performance metrics will define success?
Edge Cases

Ambiguous Queries: User inputs vague or incomplete queries. (Solution: Add clarification prompts.)
Outdated Data: Repository data might be incomplete or inaccurate. (Solution: Periodic updates and logging of access frequency.)
Phase 2: Data Preparation
Dataset Requirements

Textual Data: Organize meeting notes, strategies, PDFs, etc.
Multimedia Data: Collect charts, visuals, and other non-textual elements.
Metadata: Tag files with relevant keywords (e.g., fundraising, education).
Data Processing

Preprocess data for consistency.
Identify and remove redundancies.
Error Handling

Validate metadata structure.
Log inaccessible or corrupt files.
Phase 3: Model Implementation
Model Selection

Use OpenAI's GPT or similar models for generating responses.
Integrate a retrieval mechanism for accessing the repository.
Sample Code for RAG Setup

python
Copy code
from transformers import RagTokenizer, RagRetriever, RagSequenceForGeneration

# Initialize components
tokenizer = RagTokenizer.from_pretrained("facebook/rag-token-nq")
retriever = RagRetriever.from_pretrained("facebook/rag-token-nq", index_name="custom_index")
model = RagSequenceForGeneration.from_pretrained("facebook/rag-token-nq")

# Example query
query = "Generate ideas for fundraising campaigns"
input_ids = tokenizer(query, return_tensors="pt").input_ids

# Retrieve context
retriever_results = retriever(query)
generated_response = model.generate(input_ids=input_ids, context_input_ids=retriever_results)

print(tokenizer.decode(generated_response[0], skip_special_tokens=True))
Error Handling
Handle tokenization issues (e.g., too-long inputs).
Retry failed retrievals up to three times.
Phase 4: App Development
Frontend

Create a React-based interface for mobile and web.
Features:
Input field for queries.
File upload for adding new data.
Backend

Develop a Python-based backend using Flask or FastAPI.
Handle user queries, process data, and manage repository updates.
Logging

Log every query and response for auditing.
Sample Logging Code:
python
Copy code
import logging

logging.basicConfig(filename='queries.log', level=logging.INFO)

def log_query(user_query, ai_response):
    logging.info(f"Query: {user_query} | Response: {ai_response}")
Phase 5: Testing and Optimization
Testing

Unit Testing: Test each component individually (e.g., query handling, data retrieval).
Integration Testing: Ensure smooth interaction between frontend, backend, and AI engine.
User Testing: Gather feedback from BinaryHeart team members.
Performance Metrics

Response time: Ensure responses are generated within 3 seconds.
Accuracy: Maintain a 95% relevance rate for AI outputs.
Error Scenarios

Network Downtime: Display fallback error messages.
Corrupt Multimedia Files: Skip analysis and notify the user.
Deployment Plan
Platform

Host on a secure cloud platform (e.g., AWS, Azure).
Ensure encryption of sensitive data.
User Training

Provide training sessions and documentation.
Include FAQs and troubleshooting guides.
Conclusion
By following this PRD, the BinaryHeart AI Assistant will be a robust, efficient, and user-friendly tool for achieving BinaryHeart's goals. Through detailed logging, comprehensive error handling, and proactive testing, the assistant will address potential challenges and evolve alongside the organization.

Let me know if you need further refinements or additional details!

# PRD

Product Requirements Document (PRD): Static IMPOSSIBLE Website Conversion

1. Project Overview

Convert the existing Flask-based IMPOSSIBLE website into a static website that requires no server-side processing, making it easier to deploy and maintain.

2. Objectives

Eliminate dependency on Flask and Python

Maintain all existing functionality and design

Ensure smooth user experience

Enable easy deployment to static hosting platforms

Preserve all animations and interactive elements

3. Current Architecture 

impossible-site/

├── app.py              # Flask application (to be removed)

├── requirements.txt    # Python dependencies (to be removed)

├── static/

│   ├── css/

│   ├── js/

│   └── images/

├── templates/

│   ├── base.html

│   ├── index.html

│   ├── shop.html

│   └── contact.html

└── README.md

4. Conversion Steps

Create new project structure:

├── contact.html

Document all Flask template inheritance relationships

Document all dynamic content areas

Document all dynamic data points

<!-- Add script for scroll animations -->
<script>
    document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
        const observer = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {
            entries.forEach(entry => {
                if (entry.isIntersecting) {
                    entry.target.classList.add('slide-visible');
                }
            });
        }, {
            threshold: 0.2
        });

        // Observe all elements with animation classes
        document.querySelectorAll('.slide-from-left, .slide-from-right').forEach((el) => {
            observer.observe(el);
        });

        // Add smooth scroll behavior
        document.querySelectorAll('a[href^="#"]').forEach(anchor => {
            anchor.addEventListener('click', function (e) {
                e.preventDefault();
                const targetId = this.getAttribute('href');
                const targetElement = document.querySelector(targetId);
                if (targetElement) {
                    targetElement.scrollIntoView({
                        behavior: 'smooth',
                        block: 'start'
                    });
                }
            });
        });

        // Intersection Observer for the title
        const titleObserver = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {
            entries.forEach(entry => {
                if (entry.isIntersecting) {
                    entry.target.style.opacity = '1';
                    titleObserver.unobserve(entry.target);
                }
            });
        }, {
            threshold: 0.5
        });

        // Observe the title
        const title = document.getElementById('impossible-title');
        titleObserver.observe(title);

        // Intersection Observer for the cards
        const cardObserver = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {
            entries.forEach((entry, index) => {
                if (entry.isIntersecting) {
                    // Reduced delay between cards
                    setTimeout(() => {
                        entry.target.classList.add('visible');
                    }, index * 80); // Reduced from 150ms to 80ms delay
                    cardObserver.unobserve(entry.target);
                }
            });
        }, {
            threshold: 0.1, // Reduced threshold for earlier triggering
            rootMargin: '30px'
        });

        // Observe all acronym cards
        const cards = document.querySelectorAll('.acronym-card');
        cards.forEach((card, index) => {
            card.style.transitionDelay = `${index * 80}ms`; // Reduced delay to match
            cardObserver.observe(card);
        });

        const parallaxBg = document.getElementById('parallax-bg');
        const starsContainer = document.getElementById('stars-container');
        const stars = document.querySelectorAll('.star');
        
        // Parallax scroll effect
        window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
            const scrolled = window.pageYOffset;
            
            // Move background slower than scroll speed (0.5 = half speed)
            if (parallaxBg) {
                parallaxBg.style.transform = `translateY(${scrolled * 0.5}px)`;
            }
            
            // Move stars at different speeds for depth effect
            if (starsContainer) {
                starsContainer.style.transform = `translateY(${scrolled * 0.3}px)`;
            }
            
            // Add subtle rotation to stars while scrolling
            stars.forEach((star, index) => {
                const rotateAmount = (scrolled * 0.1 * (index + 1)) % 360;
                star.style.transform = `rotate(${rotateAmount}deg) translateY(${scrolled * 0.2}px)`;
            });
        });
    });
</script>

<!-- Add this to your script section -->
<script>
// Get all main sections
const sections = document.querySelectorAll('section');
let currentSectionIndex = 0;
let autoScrollEnabled = true;
const heroSection = sections[0]; // First section is the hero

// Function to scroll to next section
function scrollToNextSection() {
    // Find the next section that's not fully visible
    let nextSectionIndex = -1;
    sections.forEach((section, index) => {
        const rect = section.getBoundingClientRect();
        if (rect.top > 10 && nextSectionIndex === -1) {
            nextSectionIndex = index;
        }
    });

    if (nextSectionIndex !== -1) {
        sections[nextSectionIndex].scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
    }

    // Hide button after click
    hideScrollButton();
}

// Function to hide scroll button
function hideScrollButton() {
    const scrollButton = document.querySelector('.scroll-button');
    scrollButton.classList.add('opacity-0', 'pointer-events-none');
}

// Hide button and pause auto-scroll when user scrolls
window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
    // Hide button on any scroll
    hideScrollButton();
    
    // Check if we've scrolled past hero section
    const heroRect = heroSection.getBoundingClientRect();
    if (heroRect.bottom <= 0) {
        hideScrollButton();
    }
    
    autoScrollEnabled = false;
    clearInterval(autoScrollInterval);
});

// Auto scroll every 30 seconds if still in hero section
let autoScrollInterval = setInterval(() => {
    const heroRect = heroSection.getBoundingClientRect();
    if (autoScrollEnabled && heroRect.bottom > 0) {
        scrollToNextSection();
    }
}, 30000);

document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
    const parallaxBg = document.getElementById('parallax-bg');
    
    // Parallax scroll effect
    window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
        const scrolled = window.pageYOffset;
        
        // Move background slower than scroll speed (0.5 = half speed)
        if (parallaxBg) {
            parallaxBg.style.transform = `translateY(${scrolled * 0.5}px)`;
        }
    });
});

document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
    const observer = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {
        entries.forEach(entry => {
            if (entry.isIntersecting) {
                entry.target.style.opacity = '1';
                entry.target.style.transform = 'translateY(0)';
            }
        });
    }, {
        threshold: 0.1,
        rootMargin: '50px'
    });

    document.querySelectorAll('[data-timeline-item]').forEach((item) => {
        observer.observe(item);
    });
});
</script>
{% endblock %}

    <!-- Stars background with parallax -->
    <div class="absolute inset-0 w-full h-full" id="stars-bg" style="transform: translateY(0)">

<script>
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
    // Get all main sections
    const sections = document.querySelectorAll('section');
    const heroSection = sections[0]; // First section is the hero
    let autoScrollEnabled = true;

    // Function to scroll to next section
    function scrollToNextSection() {
        // Find the next section that's not fully visible
        let nextSectionIndex = -1;
        sections.forEach((section, index) => {
            const rect = section.getBoundingClientRect();
            if (rect.top > 10 && nextSectionIndex === -1) {
                nextSectionIndex = index;
            }
        });

        if (nextSectionIndex !== -1) {
            sections[nextSectionIndex].scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
        }

        // Hide button after click
        hideScrollButton();
    }

    // Function to hide scroll button
    function hideScrollButton() {
        const scrollButton = document.querySelector('.scroll-button');
        if (scrollButton) {
            scrollButton.classList.add('opacity-0', 'pointer-events-none');
        }
    }

    // Hide button and pause auto-scroll when user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
        // Hide button on any scroll
        hideScrollButton();
        
        // Check if we've scrolled past hero section
        const heroRect = heroSection.getBoundingClientRect();
        if (heroRect.bottom <= 0) {
            hideScrollButton();
        }
        
        autoScrollEnabled = false;
        clearInterval(autoScrollInterval);
    });

    // Auto scroll every 30 seconds if still in hero section
    let autoScrollInterval = setInterval(() => {
        const heroRect = heroSection.getBoundingClientRect();
        if (autoScrollEnabled && heroRect.bottom > 0) {
            scrollToNextSection();
        }
    }, 30000);

    // Make scrollToNextSection available globally
    window.scrollToNextSection = scrollToNextSection;
});
</script>

<script>
let currentSlide = 0;
const totalSlides = 11;
const carousel = document.getElementById('carousel');
const slides = Array.from(carousel.children);

// Add touch handling variables
let touchStartX = 0;
let touchEndX = 0;
const minSwipeDistance = 50; // Minimum distance for a swipe

// Add touch event listeners
carousel.addEventListener('touchstart', (e) => {
    touchStartX = e.touches[0].clientX;
});

carousel.addEventListener('touchmove', (e) => {
    touchEndX = e.touches[0].clientX;
});

carousel.addEventListener('touchend', () => {
    handleSwipe();
});

// Handle the swipe
function handleSwipe() {
    const swipeDistance = touchEndX - touchStartX;
    
    if (Math.abs(swipeDistance) > minSwipeDistance) {
        if (swipeDistance > 0) {
            // Swiped right - go to previous slide
            moveCarousel(1);
        } else {
            // Swiped left - go to next slide
            moveCarousel(-1);
        }
    }
    
    // Reset touch coordinates
    touchStartX = 0;
    touchEndX = 0;
}

function updateCarousel() {
    const isMobile = window.innerWidth < 768;
    const slideWidth = isMobile ? window.innerWidth * 0.8 : 800;
    const peekAmount = isMobile ? 50 : 150;
    
    slides.forEach((slide, index) => {
        let position = index - currentSlide;
        
        // Handle wrapping
        if (position < -Math.floor(slides.length/2)) {
            position += slides.length;
        } else if (position > Math.floor(slides.length/2)) {
            position -= slides.length;
        }
        
        // Calculate transform values
        let xPos = 0;
        let scale = 0;
        let opacity = 0;
        let zIndex = 0;
        let rotateY = 0;
        
        if (position === 0) {
            // Current slide
            xPos = 0;
            scale = 1;
            opacity = 1;
            zIndex = 10;
            rotateY = 0;
            slide.classList.add('active');
        } else if (position === -1 || position === slides.length - 1) {
            // Left adjacent slide
            xPos = -(slideWidth - peekAmount);
            scale = isMobile ? 0.7 : 0.8;
            opacity = 0.6;
            zIndex = 5;
            rotateY = 15;
            slide.classList.remove('active');
        } else if (position === 1 || position === -(slides.length - 1)) {
            // Right adjacent slide
            xPos = (slideWidth - peekAmount);
            scale = isMobile ? 0.7 : 0.8;
            opacity = 0.6;
            zIndex = 5;
            rotateY = -15;
            slide.classList.remove('active');
        } else {
            // Hidden slides
            xPos = position < 0 ? -slideWidth : slideWidth;
            scale = isMobile ? 0.5 : 0.6;
            opacity = 0;
            zIndex = 1;
            rotateY = position < 0 ? 30 : -30;
            slide.classList.remove('active');
        }
        
        slide.style.transform = `translateX(${xPos}px) scale(${scale}) rotateY(${rotateY}deg)`;
        slide.style.opacity = opacity;
        slide.style.zIndex = zIndex;
    });
}

function moveCarousel(direction) {
    currentSlide = (currentSlide - direction + slides.length) % slides.length;
    updateCarousel();
}

// Add click handlers to all images
slides.forEach((slide, index) => {
    slide.addEventListener('click', () => {
        if (index !== currentSlide) {
            const distance = index - currentSlide;
            const shortestPath = distance > slides.length/2 ? distance - slides.length : 
                               distance < -slides.length/2 ? distance + slides.length : distance;
            currentSlide = index;
            updateCarousel();
        }
    });
});

// Optional: Auto-advance slides
let autoAdvance = setInterval(() => moveCarousel(-1), 5000);

// Pause auto-advance on hover
carousel.parentElement.addEventListener('mouseenter', () => clearInterval(autoAdvance));
carousel.parentElement.addEventListener('mouseleave', () => {
    autoAdvance = setInterval(() => moveCarousel(-1), 5000);
});

// Initialize carousel
updateCarousel();

document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
    const starsBg = document.getElementById('stars-bg');
    const earthParallax = document.getElementById('earth-parallax');
    
    // Parallax scroll effect
    window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
        const scrolled = window.pageYOffset;
        
        // Move stars slower than scroll speed (0.3 = 30% speed)
        if (starsBg) {
            starsBg.style.transform = `translateY(${scrolled * 0.3}px)`;
        }
        
        // Move earth at a different speed and add slight rotation
        if (earthParallax) {
            const rotation = scrolled * 0.02; // Very subtle rotation
            earthParallax.style.transform = `translateY(${scrolled * 0.4}px) rotate(${rotation}deg)`;
        }
    });

    // ... rest of your existing script ...
});
</script>

    }

        transition: transform 0.3s ease-out;
    }

        animation: pulse 2s infinite;

<!-- Add required scripts -->
<script>
    // Scroll animation
    const scrollElements = document.querySelectorAll('.scroll-fade');

    const elementInView = (el) => {
        const elementTop = el.getBoundingClientRect().top;
        return elementTop <= (window.innerHeight || document.documentElement.clientHeight) * 0.8;
    };

    const displayScrollElement = (element) => {
        element.classList.add('visible');
    };

    const handleScrollAnimation = () => {
        scrollElements.forEach((el) => {
            if (elementInView(el)) {
                displayScrollElement(el);
            }
        });
    };

    window.addEventListener('scroll', handleScrollAnimation);
    window.addEventListener('load', handleScrollAnimation);

    // Star field animation
    const canvas = document.getElementById('particleCanvas');
    const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');
    let width = canvas.width = window.innerWidth;
    let height = canvas.height = window.innerHeight;
    let mouseX = width / 2;
    let mouseY = height / 2;

    // Star class
    class Star {
        constructor() {
            this.x = Math.random() * width;
            this.y = Math.random() * height;
            this.size = Math.random() * 1.5 + 0.5; // Random size between 0.5 and 2
            this.baseSize = this.size;
        }

        draw() {
            const dx = mouseX - this.x;
            const dy = mouseY - this.y;
            const distance = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);
            const maxDistance = 150; // Maximum distance for elongation effect
            
            // Calculate elongation based on distance (reduced effect)
            const elongation = Math.max(0, 1 - distance / maxDistance) * 0.5; // Reduced elongation multiplier
            const angle = Math.atan2(dy, dx);
            
            // Save the current context state
            ctx.save();
            
            // Move to star's position and rotate towards cursor
            ctx.translate(this.x, this.y);
            ctx.rotate(angle);
            
            // Draw elongated star with constant opacity
            ctx.fillStyle = 'rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.3)'; // Lower constant opacity
            ctx.beginPath();
            
            // Calculate elongation scale (reduced)
            const scaleX = 1 + elongation * 1.5; // Reduced max elongation
            const scaleY = 1;
            
            // Draw elongated circle
            ctx.ellipse(0, 0, this.size * scaleX, this.size * scaleY, 0, 0, Math.PI * 2);
            ctx.fill();
            
            // Restore the context state
            ctx.restore();
        }
    }

    // Initialize stars
    const stars = [];
    const numberOfStars = 300;

    function init() {
        stars.length = 0; // Clear existing stars
        for (let i = 0; i < numberOfStars; i++) {
            stars.push(new Star());
        }
    }

    function animate() {
        ctx.clearRect(0, 0, width, height);
        stars.forEach(star => star.draw());
        requestAnimationFrame(animate);
    }

    // Handle mouse movement
    window.addEventListener('mousemove', (e) => {
        mouseX = e.x;
        mouseY = e.y;
    });

    // Handle window resize
    window.addEventListener('resize', () => {
        width = canvas.width = window.innerWidth;
        height = canvas.height = window.innerHeight;
        init();
    });

    // Initialize and start animation
    init();
    animate();

    // Get all main sections
    const sections = document.querySelectorAll('section');
    let currentSectionIndex = 0;
    let autoScrollEnabled = true;
    const heroSection = sections[0]; // First section is the hero

    // Function to scroll to next section
    function scrollToNextSection() {
        // Find the next section that's not fully visible
        let nextSectionIndex = -1;
        sections.forEach((section, index) => {
            const rect = section.getBoundingClientRect();
            if (rect.top > 10 && nextSectionIndex === -1) {
                nextSectionIndex = index;
            }
        });

        if (nextSectionIndex !== -1) {
            sections[nextSectionIndex].scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
        }

        // Hide button after click
        hideScrollButton();
    }

    // Function to hide scroll button
    function hideScrollButton() {
        const scrollButton = document.querySelector('.scroll-button');
        if (scrollButton) {
            scrollButton.classList.add('opacity-0', 'pointer-events-none');
        }
    }

    // Hide button and pause auto-scroll when user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', () => {
        // Hide button on any scroll
        hideScrollButton();
        
        // Check if we've scrolled past hero section
        const heroRect = heroSection.getBoundingClientRect();
        if (heroRect.bottom <= 0) {
            hideScrollButton();
        }
        
        autoScrollEnabled = false;
        clearInterval(autoScrollInterval);
    });

    // Auto scroll every 30 seconds if still in hero section
    let autoScrollInterval = setInterval(() => {
        const heroRect = heroSection.getBoundingClientRect();
        if (autoScrollEnabled && heroRect.bottom > 0) {
            scrollToNextSection();
        }
    }, 30000);
</script>
{% endblock %}

    <script>
        // Load header and footer
        fetch('base.html')
            .then(response => response.text())
            .then(html => {
                const parser = new DOMParser();
                const doc = parser.parseFromString(html, 'text/html');
                
                // Extract header
                const header = doc.querySelector('header');
                document.getElementById('header').innerHTML = header.outerHTML;
                
                // Extract footer
                const footer = doc.querySelector('footer');
                document.getElementById('footer').innerHTML = footer.outerHTML;
            });

        // Load and display products
        fetch('data/products.json')
            .then(response => response.json())
            .then(data => {
                const productGrid = document.getElementById('productGrid');
                data.products.forEach(product => {
                    const card = createProductCard(product);
                    productGrid.appendChild(card);
                });
            })
            .catch(error => console.error('Error loading products:', error));

        // Product card creation
        function createProductCard(product) {
            const card = document.createElement('div');
            card.className = 'bg-[#0f1219] rounded-xl shadow-lg overflow-hidden transform transition-all duration-300 hover:-translate-y-1 hover:shadow-xl border border-gray-800';
            
            const formattedPrice = (product.base_price / 100).toFixed(2);
            const defaultImage = product.images[Object.keys(product.images)[0]].front;
            
            card.innerHTML = `
                <div class="aspect-w-4 aspect-h-3">
                    <img src="${defaultImage}" alt="${product.name}" class="w-full h-full object-contain">
                </div>
                <div class="p-6">
                    <h3 class="text-xl font-bold text-white mb-2">${product.name}</h3>
                    <p class="text-gray-300 text-base mb-4">${product.description}</p>
                    <div class="flex justify-between items-center">
                        <span class="text-lg font-semibold text-white">$${formattedPrice}</span>
                        <button onclick="openProductModal('${product.id}')" class="bg-blue-500 text-white px-6 py-2 rounded-lg font-semibold hover:bg-blue-600 transition-all duration-300">
                            View Details
                        </button>
                    </div>
                </div>
            `;
            return card;
        }
    </script>

# PRD

Product Requirements Document: Local File RAG System
1. Introduction/Overview

This document outlines the requirements for a local file Retrieval Augmented Generation (RAG) system. The system will allow users to upload files to a local directory, index them, and then use a large language model (LLM) to answer questions based on the content of those files. The system will prioritize maintaining file structure, semantic search, cost-effectiveness, and leveraging available resources like Azure credits and student discounts.

2. Goals

Enable efficient and accurate question answering based on local file content.
Preserve and utilize file structure for context and search.
Support a wide range of common file formats.
Minimize costs by leveraging free resources and optimizing for efficiency.
Provide a user-friendly experience.
3. Target Audience

Students
Researchers
Individuals managing large local document collections
4. Scope

This project will focus on building a local, desktop-based RAG system. It will not include features like cloud hosting, user accounts, or collaborative editing in the initial phase.

5. Functional Requirements

File Upload and Indexing:
Users can specify a local directory containing their files.
The system recursively indexes all files within the directory and its subdirectories.
Supported file formats: pptx, markdown, csv, html, pdf, docx, xlsx, txt, and other common formats.
File metadata (name, path, size, modification date) is stored and used for context.
File content is extracted and converted to a suitable format for the LLM (e.g., plain text).
The indexing process should be efficient and handle large numbers of files.
Semantic Search:
Users can input natural language queries.
The system performs a semantic search over the indexed content to find relevant passages.
Search should consider file names, paths, and content.
Results are ranked by relevance.
Context Retrieval and LLM Interaction:
The system retrieves the most relevant passages based on the search results.
The retrieved context, along with a user-defined system prompt and the user's query, is passed to the LLM.
The LLM generates a response based on the provided context.
System Prompt:
Users can define a system prompt to guide the LLM's behavior (e.g., specifying a role or tone).
Output Display:
The LLM's response is displayed to the user.
The system optionally displays the source files or passages used to generate the response.
Configuration:
Users should be able to configure parameters such as the LLM model, embedding model, and chunk size.
6. Non-Functional Requirements

Performance: The system should index files and respond to queries in a reasonable time.
Scalability: The system should be able to handle a large number of files.
Usability: The system should be easy to use and understand.
Cost-Effectiveness: The system should minimize costs by leveraging free resources and optimizing for efficiency.
Maintainability: The system should be well-structured and easy to maintain.
7. Technical Requirements

Programming Language: Python (due to extensive libraries for NLP and file processing)
LLM: Azure OpenAI Service (leveraging free credits) or local LLMs like llama.cpp (for cost-effectiveness)
Embedding Model: Sentence Transformers (open-source and efficient) or Azure OpenAI Embeddings (if budget allows)
Vector Database/Index: FAISS (Facebook AI Similarity Search) or Chroma (open source) for efficient similarity search.
File Parsing Libraries: Libraries like Apache Tika, PyPDF2, python-pptx, etc., for extracting text from various file formats.
8. Cost Considerations

Prioritize using free tiers and open-source solutions wherever possible.
Leverage Azure free credits for Azure OpenAI API calls.
Consider running smaller LLMs locally to reduce API costs.
Optimize embedding and search processes to minimize API usage.
9. Open Issues/Risks

Handling very large files or extremely large document collections might require further optimization.
Maintaining accurate file structure representation in the vector database needs careful design.
10. Future Considerations

Integration with cloud storage services.
User authentication and authorization.
Collaborative features.
Graphical User Interface (GUI).
================================================================================

# Hiding search bar thru pwa

I wantit so that the search bar at the bottom of browsers compresses like when you scroll down whenever you get on the site automatically on mobile browsers. I think something like this might work: 1. Turn the site into a PWA and run it full-screen
If you add a Web-App Manifest and the correct iOS meta tags, the bar disappears after the user adds your site to their Home Screen and launches it from there.

<link rel="manifest" href="/site.webmanifest">

# PRD

Product Requirements Document (PRD)
Project: Social Media Clipping Platform
Overview
A simple, user-friendly website for casual users to upload or import audio/video files (or TikTok/YouTube links) and quickly create clips for social media. The platform will automatically convert files to standard formats (mp3/mp4) and offer an intuitive timeline interface for clipping, trimming, merging, and downloading segments.

Objectives
Simplicity: Provide an extremely easy-to-use interface tailored for casual users.

Speed: Allow quick clipping and sharing of media for social media use.

Efficiency: Automatically handle file conversion for seamless user experience.

Target Audience
Primary Users: Casual users seeking a fast, straightforward solution for clipping and sharing media on social platforms.

Key Features & Functionality
File Input & Conversion:

Uploads: Accept any audio/video file (no size/duration limits).

Link Import: Allow users to import TikTok/YouTube links.

Automatic Conversion: Automatically convert imported files/links to mp3/mp4 (or other standard formats) without user intervention.

Clipping & Editing:

Timeline Interface:

Visual timeline for users to select clip start and end times.

Drag-and-drop handles to adjust clip boundaries.

Overlapping clips are allowed.

Editing Tools:

Trim clips.

Delete unwanted segments.

Merge clips.

Create and download clips.

Real-Time Preview:

Full file viewer with playback controls.

Video playback tracks as clip boundaries are adjusted.

For audio files, a simple black screen with an audio waveform or playback indicator.

Saving & User Management:

Temporary Storage: Clips are stored only for the session; once the user leaves the page, clips are deleted.

User Registration: Simple signup/login with username and password to facilitate the session and enable clip downloads.

UI/UX:

Simplicity: A clean, straightforward interface with minimal clutter.

Multi-Page Flow:

Upload/Import Screen: For file uploads and entering TikTok/YouTube links.

Editing Screen: Dedicated to timeline-based clipping and editing.

Responsive Design: Ensuring a smooth experience on both desktop and mobile devices.

Technical Requirements
Frontend:

Implement using modern web technologies.

Use a robust timeline library or custom JavaScript solution for clip editing.

Ensure responsive design for multiple devices.

Backend:

Handle file uploads, conversion (using tools like FFmpeg), and temporary storage.

User authentication for simple registration and login.

Manage session data to automatically clear clips when a user exits.

Conversion & Processing:

Automatic conversion of various audio/video formats to standardized formats (mp3/mp4) upon upload or link import.

Efficient processing pipeline to ensure quick turnaround for conversion and editing.

Dependencies & Assumptions
Rely on established libraries/tools for file conversion (e.g., FFmpeg).

The temporary storage model assumes users download their clips before exiting.

Platform will initially support TikTok/YouTube links only; other platforms may be considered in the future.

Out-of-Scope (for MVP)
Social sharing features (beyond download).

Monetization, ads, or an admin panel.

Advanced security measures like file scanning or watermarking.

Timeline & Milestones
Phase 1 – MVP Development:

Set up file upload/import functionality.

Implement automatic file conversion.

Develop the basic timeline editor with clip trimming, deletion, merging, and download options.

Integrate simple user registration/login.

Phase 2 – UI/UX Refinements:

Enhance the timeline interface and real-time preview functionality.

Improve responsiveness and cross-device compatibility.

Phase 3 – Testing & Launch:

Conduct user testing and iterate based on feedback.

Optimize performance and stability.

Launch the platform.
================================================================================

# PRD

Absolutely — here is a clean, comprehensive PRD (Product Requirements Document) for your project — written like you'd hand it to a dev agency or AI product builder.

---

# PRD — Kids Guitar Learning Website  
## Working Name: *GuitarQuest*  
*"Learn to play like a Rockstar (without feeling like homework)"*

---

## 1. Objective

Create a web-based, interactive guitar learning platform designed specifically for kids ages 7-14. The product should blend game mechanics, fun animated teaching, and structured musical progression to create the most delightful first guitar experience possible.

This product is not an app store app — it is a mobile-optimized website that functions like a game. 

---

## 2. Target Audience

| Audience | Details |
|-----------|---------|
| Primary | Kids ages 7-14 with little to no guitar experience |
| Secondary | Parents looking for screen time that feels educational & creative |
| Tertiary | Music teachers seeking classroom-friendly beginner tools |

---

## 3. Core Product Goals

| Goal | Success Metric |
|------|----------------|
| Kids learn enough to play their first real song in under 1 week | % of users completing first song module |
| Kids stay engaged and come back repeatedly | Avg. sessions per week per user |
| Experience feels like a game, not a lesson | User retention & qualitative feedback |
| Visual, audio, and interactivity optimized for fun & simplicity | Completion rate of early levels |

---

## 4. Product Features & Requirements

### 4.1 Lesson Structure & World Map
- The user moves through "Worlds" like levels in a game.
- Worlds are themed learning modules.
- XP Points unlock progress.

| World | Lessons Focus | Unlock Condition |
|-------|----------------|------------------|
| 1. Guitar Basics World | Holding, parts of guitar, tuning | Automatic start |
| 2. First Sounds World | Single string riffs | Complete Basics World |
| 3. Chords World | Simple chords, power chords | Earn 500 XP |
| 4. Rhythm World | Strumming patterns, clapping games | Earn 1000 XP |
| 5. Song World | Play simple full songs | Complete Chords World |
| 6. Jam World | Improv & play-along tracks | Bonus content |

---

- Level system with rewards every level up.

# PRD

1. Purpose
Enable users to seamlessly transfer files between a phone and a computer (or any other device) with minimal friction. The system should offer both internet-based and wired transfer options, detecting cables automatically when present. Files are accessible via a temporary web interface (5-minute availability window).

2. Overview
Web-based Interface: Accessible from any browser.
Cross-Platform: Works on mobile, desktop, and tablet.
Simple Authentication: Username/password or similar credential.
Time-Limited Availability: Files expire 5 minutes after upload.
Auto Cable Detection: If a physical cable is plugged in, transfer happens locally, bypassing internet.
3. Goals & Objectives
Ease of Use: Single-click or minimal steps to start transferring files.
Speed & Efficiency: Automatically choose the fastest method (wired vs. internet).
Security: Basic authentication to ensure only intended users can access uploaded files.
Simplicity in Deployment: Lightweight solution that can be hosted easily on a local or cloud server.
4. User Stories
Upload and Download (Internet):

As a user, I can drag-and-drop a file into a web page on my phone.
Then, from my computer browser, I log in with the same credentials.
So that, I can see the file and download it within 5 minutes.
Cable Transfer:

As a user, if I plug my phone into my computer via a cable, the system detects the cable automatically.
Then, it routes file transfers through the cable, offering higher speeds and bypassing the internet.
Auto-Expiration:

As a user, I can rest assured that any files I upload will be automatically removed after 5 minutes, ensuring minimal data retention.
5. Functional Requirements
File Upload and Download

Must support any file type (e.g., images, documents, videos, etc.).
Files can be uploaded via drag-and-drop or a “Select File” button.
Progress bar or status indicator for large file uploads.
Time-Limited Availability

Each uploaded file is stored for 5 minutes.
Countdown timer is displayed in the UI, after which the file is deleted automatically.
Authentication

Simple username and password to access the web interface.
Option to store credentials locally for repeated use (session-based).
Cable Detection

Automatically detect if the device is connected by cable (e.g., USB).
If connected, route file transfer over USB instead of the internet.
Show a clear indication in the UI that cable transfer is active.
Web Interface

Responsive design for desktop and mobile browsers.
Minimal steps for file transfer (upload, wait, download).
6. Non-Functional Requirements
Performance

Handle files up to a certain maximum size (to be defined by server capacity).
Efficiently manage large files when cable is not available (e.g., chunked uploads).
Security

HTTPS support for web interface (SSL/TLS).
Securely store user credentials (hashed + salted if in a database).
Implement token-based session management or similar to prevent unauthorized access.
Scalability

Ability to handle concurrent uploads from multiple users if needed.
Storage should clean up expired files to prevent accumulation.
Maintainability

Clear separation of front-end (web UI) and back-end (file handling, cable detection).
Code documentation for easy handover to other developers.
7. Technical Approach
Architecture

Front-End: Single-page web application (SPA) or lightweight HTML/JS.
Back-End: Node.js, Python, or similar framework with REST endpoints.
Database/Storage:
In-memory or temporary storage (e.g., Redis, or local file system with a cleanup script) for file expiration.
Optionally store metadata (filename, upload time) for the 5-minute lifecycle.
Cable Detection

Utilize system-level APIs or platform-specific libraries (e.g., for USB detection in Node.js or Python).
Fallback to internet if no cable is detected.
File Transfer Protocol

For internet: Standard HTTPS uploads (multipart form-data).
For cable: Use an OS-level mounting or direct data transfer method (e.g., MTP for Android, iTunes File Sharing for iOS, or direct USB mass storage if supported).
Expiration Mechanism

Background job or scheduled task to check for files older than 5 minutes and remove them.
Update the UI with a countdown timer.
8. User Interface / User Experience
Login Screen:

Username + Password fields.
“Remember Me” checkbox (optional).
Main Dashboard:

Drag-and-drop zone + “Upload File” button.
List of uploaded files with time remaining.
Download button for each file.
Cable Transfer Indicator:

Icon or text message (“Cable Detected” / “Cable Transfer Active”).
Error Handling:

Show messages for unsupported file size or file type if limitations apply.
Display network or cable errors gracefully.
9. Security & Privacy
Secure Connections:

All transfers over HTTPS or a secure cable connection.
SSL certificate on the server.
Data Retention:

Files auto-delete after 5 minutes.
No logs of file contents stored beyond that period.
Access Control:

Only authenticated sessions can upload/download.
Session ends on logout or inactivity timeout.
10. Edge Cases
User Closes Browser Mid-Upload:
Partial uploads are discarded.
Network Interruption:
System retries if feasible; otherwise, user must re-initiate upload.
Cable Not Supported by OS:
Fallback to internet-based transfer.
Large Files
If file exceeds a certain size (defined by server capacity), system should prompt an error or chunk the upload.
11. Testing & QA
Unit Tests for each back-end component (upload, file deletion, cable detection).
Integration Tests for end-to-end file upload/download and time expiration.
UI Tests to ensure consistent behavior on various browsers/devices.
Security Testing to confirm encryption, authentication, and vulnerability checks.
================================================================================

# PRD

1 — Purpose & Vision
Ship a fully open‑source, Windows‑only desktop tool that records every mouse/keyboard interaction after sign‑in, snapshots the screen, draws a numbered circle on each click, lets the user reorder/delete/label steps, and exports a polished DOCX or PDF guide—all built on the mature Electron + Node.js ecosystem for speed of development and contributor familiarity.

2 — Goals / Non‑Goals

In Scope (v1)	Out of Scope (v1)
Recording	Global mouse clicks & keyboard shortcuts	Continuous video/audio, multi‑monitor capture
Screenshots	Full‑screen PNG per click	Region capture, OCR, auto‑blur
Annotation	Auto circle + step number on every PNG	Ripple effects, animated call‑outs
Editing	Re‑order & delete steps, edit title/description	Step merge, version history
Export	DOCX & PDF with embedded images	Cloud sync, integrations (Notion, Confluence, …)
Platforms	Windows 10+ desktop (.exe / installer)	macOS, Linux, mobile
3 — User Personas
Ops Trainer: create SOPs for new hires weekly.

Tech Support Rep: one‑off how‑to docs for customers.

QA Analyst: attach repro steps to Jira tickets daily.

Student Dev: contribute translations/features via GitHub.

4 — Functional Requirements
4.1 Recording Engine
Start/Pause/Stop via floating bar or Ctrl + Shift + R / P / S.

Hook global mouse/keyboard using iohook.

After each click/shortcut:

Capture full screen with screenshot‑desktop → PNG.

Draw 24 px red circle + white index (#) at click coords via sharp.

Persist step {id, title, desc, timestamp, pngPath, windowTitle, keyCombo?} to local JSON.

4.2 Editor UI
Sidebar list (drag‑n‑drop ↓↑), step thumbnail, inline title & rich‑text description.

Delete button with confirmation.

Manual rectangular Blur Tool overlay stored as SVG path (future proof).

4.3 Export Module
DOCX generation with docx npm; template:

makefile
Copy
Edit
Heading 1: Step N — {Title}
Image: PNG scaled to 6.5"
Body: Description
PDF via docx-pdf or headless LibreOffice on user system.

File names: OpenScribe_{YYYY‑MM‑DD_HH‑MM‑SS}.{docx|pdf}.

4.4 Settings
Circle colour/size, hotkeys, default export dir, keyboard capture toggle.

5 — Non‑Functional Requirements

Category	Requirement
Performance	≤ 300 MB RAM on 8 GB laptop for 500‑step session; CPU < 20 % avg during record
Reliability	Zero missed clicks in 2000‑step stress test
Security	No outbound network traffic without explicit opt‑in update‑check
Distribution	Signed NSIS installer & portable ZIP; auto‑update via Electron‑updater
Accessibility	All UI reachable with keyboard; high‑contrast theme
6 — Technical Architecture
java
Copy
Edit
Electron Main (Node.js)
│
├─ iohook (native C++ add‑on) ──▶ click / key events
│
├─ screenshot‑desktop ─▶ raw PNG
│                        │
│                        └─ sharp ─▶ circle overlay
│
└─ IPC (Electron) ◀───── Renderer (React + Redux/Zustand)
                         ├─ RecordingBar.tsx
                         ├─ Editor/
                         ├─ Settings/
                         └─ Export service (docx, pdf-lib)
7 — Stack & Dependencies

Layer	Choice / Libs	Rationale
Desktop Shell	Electron 28+	Ubiquitous, fast dev cycle, hot reload
Hooks	iohook (maintained fork)	Stable global mouse & KB hooks on Windows
Capture	screenshot‑desktop	Uses built‑in GDI; avoids ffmpeg dependency
Image Editing	sharp	Fast native lib, supports drawing & blur
State Mgmt	Zustand (tiny)	Simple global store
UI Kit	Shadcn/ui + Tailwind	Quick styling
Doc Export	docx, docx-pdf	Pure JS, no MS Word required
Packaging	electron-builder + NSIS	Produces signed installer & portable exe
Tests	Jest + Playwright (e2e)	GUI regression
8 — Repository & OSS Governance

Item	Decision
Repo	github.com/OpenScribe/openscribe-electron
License	MIT
Branching	main + feature branches + semantic tags
CI/CD	GitHub Actions: lint, test, build, sign
Contributions	Issues → PR → reviewer checklist
Code of Conduct	Contributor Covenant v2.1
9 — Milestones

Date (2025)	Deliverable
May 01	POC: hook clicks, capture PNG, draw circle
May 20	Alpha: RecordingBar UI + JSON step list
Jun 15	Beta: Editor (reorder/delete), DOCX export
Jul 05	RC1: PDF export, settings panel, signed installer
Jul 20	v1.0 public release on GitHub & Chocolatey
Q3	Community backlog triage (region capture, plugins)
10 — Acceptance Criteria
End‑to‑end flow

Record 15 clicks → edit titles/descriptions → delete 2 steps → export DOCX & PDF.

Both files open in Word/Acrobat with correct images & numbering.

Resource usage

500‑click session stays under 300 MB RAM / 20 % CPU on 8 GB machine.

Data privacy

Running netstat shows no open outbound connections during record/export.

Installer

NSIS installer registers Start‑menu shortcut, no admin rights needed, uninstaller cleans all files.

# Outline to fix project bar

Thought for 4 seconds

### Goal

Build a *true* project‑based tutorial manager so users can keep the recordings, steps, and exports for each workflow totally separate (e.g., **“Download a File”**, **“Print a Page”**, **“Install an App”**).

---

## 1. Data Model

| Object          | Key Fields                                                                            | Relationships                                        | Notes                                      |
| --------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------ |
| **Project**     | `id`, `name`, `createdAt`, `updatedAt`, optional `description`, `tags[]`              | Has many **Tutorials**                               | Top‑level folder shown in sidebar          |
| **Tutorial**    | `id`, `projectId`, `title`, `status` (draft/ready/exported), `createdAt`, `updatedAt` | Has many **Steps**                                   | One screen‑capture session == one tutorial |
| **Step**        | `id`, `tutorialId`, `order`, `screenshotPath`, `actionText`, `timestamp`              | Belongs to one Tutorial                              | Auto‑captured or manually added            |
| **Asset** (opt) | `id`, `tutorialId`, `type`, `path/url`                                                | Links to any extra files (audio, video, attachments) | Keeps filesystem tidy                      |

**Storage:**

* SQLite / low‑overhead DB for metadata
* Screenshot files stored in `~/OpenScribe/{projectName}/{tutorialName}/steps/`

---

## 2. Sidebar Behaviour

| Section      | What It Shows                                            | Interactions                                                                                                                              |
| ------------ | -------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Projects** | last‑opened first | • Click = open project and list its tutorials in center pane<br>• Right‑click = context menu (rename, duplicate, delete, export, archive) |
| **Recent**   | Last 5–10 tutorials across *all* projects                | • Click = jump straight to tutorial view (skipping project browse)                                                                        |

**Additions**

* “•••” kebab at bottom ⇒ *Manage Projects* (bulk reorder, search, import/export)
* Collapsible groups when project count > 10 (use disclosure triangles)
* Hover tooltip with project description + last edited date

---

## 3. Main Workspace Flow

1. **Create Project**

   * `+ New Project` button → prompt for name (and optional description)
   * App creates directory & DB entry

2. **Within a Project**

   * Center pane switches from *Screen Recording* to a list/grid of tutorials
   * “+ New Tutorial” big button (or keep the current Record card but scoped)

3. **Recording**

   * On **Start Recording**, user must choose which project *and* give a tutorial title **before** capture begins (default to open project)
   * Steps and screenshots auto‑saved to project folder live (autosave‑every‑step)

4. **Editing Steps**

   * Selecting a tutorial opens Step Editor tab (reuse your *Edit Steps* UI)
   * All edits write back to DB; thumbnails update in real‑time

5. **Exporting**

   * Export button now exports **this tutorial only** (PDF/HTML/Markdown)
   * Batch export: right‑click project → *Export Project → zip or merged PDF*

---

## 4. Command Palette / Shortcuts

| Action                              | Shortcut           |
| ----------------------------------- | ------------------ |
| New Project                         | **Ctrl+Alt+N**     |
| New Tutorial (in open project)      | **Ctrl+Alt+T**     |
| Switch Project                      | **Ctrl+Alt+⇧ Tab** |
| Quick Search (projects + tutorials) | **Ctrl+Alt+F**     |

---

## 5. Autosave & Versioning

* **Autosave every action**: never lose steps if the app crashes
* Lightweight diff: when editing a step, keep previous version for *Undo* history (10 levels)
* Option in *Advanced Settings* → “Keep step history” (toggle for power users)

---

## 6. Edge‑Case Handling

| Scenario                              | Behavior                                                          |
| ------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Deleting a Project                    | Warn: “This will delete 3 tutorials and 97 screenshots (120 MB).” |
| Recording without selecting a project | Force user to pick/create before “Start Recording” lights up      |
| Duplicate names                       | Append “(2)” or block with inline error                           |
| Moving tutorial to another project    | In context menu → *Move to…* (updates DB & moves files)           |

---

## 7. Future Nice‑to‑Haves (Backlog)

1. **Tags & Filters** (e.g., “Windows”, “Mac”, “Onboarding”)
2. **Team Collaboration** (sync projects via cloud drive or Git)
3. **Template Tutorials** (pre‑filled step skeletons)
4. **Global Analytics Dashboard** (steps recorded, time saved)

---

### Implementation Order

1. **DB schema + file structure**
2. **Project CRUD UI in sidebar**
3. **Tutorial list view inside project**
4. **Scoped recording & autosave**
5. **Move/delete/export flows**
6. Polish (search, shortcuts, tooltips)

---

This structure keeps the UX simple while giving you robust project separation and room to scale.

---

# Project Overview

# **Trace (OpenScribe) - Application Summary**

## **The Problem**
Creating comprehensive documentation and training materials is a time-consuming, manual process that often results in inconsistent, outdated guides. Teams struggle to capture institutional knowledge effectively, especially when documenting software workflows or complex processes. Traditional methods involve taking scattered screenshots, writing separate instructions, and manually formatting everything into coherent documentation - a process that's both tedious and error-prone.

## **The Solution**
OpenScribe is a desktop application that automates the entire documentation creation process through intelligent screen recording and annotation. It captures your workflow as you perform it, automatically taking screenshots at key moments and organizing them into structured, step-by-step tutorials. The application eliminates the manual work of screenshot capture, formatting, and document assembly while ensuring consistency across all documentation.

## **How It Works**
The application runs in the background, intelligently capturing screenshots when you click or press Enter, using advanced buffering to ensure clean captures without UI transitions. You can then enhance these captured steps with professional annotations like arrows, highlights, and callouts. The workflow is organized into projects and tutorials, with each step automatically timestamped and linked to relevant context like window titles and keyboard shortcuts.

## **What It Can Do**
OpenScribe enables teams to create professional training materials, process documentation, and user guides that can be exported as polished PDF or Word documents. It supports unlimited projects and tutorials (depending on license tier), persistent markup annotations, and customizable export options. The application includes a subscription-based licensing system with offline support, making it suitable for both individual users and enterprise teams who need to systematically capture and share knowledge across their organization.

# New Notepad

keystroke tracking

# Licensing

Perfect — tying the license to a **user account** is the most flexible and secure method, especially for monthly billing and multi-device handling. Here's a complete system design tailored for you:

---

## **A. System Overview**

You’ll need:

1. **Authentication system** (email/password or OAuth)
2. **License server** to track accounts and billing status
3. **Client-side enforcement** (your local app)
4. **Monthly license checks** and optional offline support

---

## **B. User Flow**

### 1. **User Signup & Payment**

* User creates an account on your website or in the app.
* Connect to Stripe, Paddle, or LemonSqueezy for monthly billing.
* On payment success, your backend sets `license_status = active`.

### 2. **App Login**

* User logs in to the app with credentials.
* App sends a request to your license server:

  ```
  POST /auth/login { email, password }
  → returns access_token + license_status
  ```
* Store `access_token` securely (with expiration).

### 3. **License Check on Launch**

* On every app start:

  * Send:

    ```json
    GET /license/check
    Authorization: Bearer access_token
    Payload: { machine_id }
    ```
  * Server verifies:

    * Account status (`active`, `cancelled`, `past_due`)
    * Machine binding (limit 1–2 machines, unless upgraded)

### 4. **Allow Limited Offline Use**

* Store a signed token (e.g., JWT) with license expiry.
* Allow use without internet for 3–5 days max.
* On reconnection, refresh the token.

---

## **C. License Server Design**

Your backend should track:

| Field            | Example                                     |
| ---------------- | ------------------------------------------- |
| `user_id`        | UUID                                        |
| `email`          | [user@example.com](mailto:user@example.com) |
| `license_status` | `active` / `past_due` / `revoked`           |
| `expires_at`     | 2025-06-18T00:00:00Z                        |
| `machine_ids`    | \[hash1, hash2]                             |

### Key Routes:

* `POST /auth/login`
* `GET /license/check`
* `POST /license/activate`
* `POST /license/deactivate`

---

## **D. Preventing Abuse**

* **Machine binding**: Generate a machine hash (e.g., MAC + OS + CPU)
* **Rate limit activations**: e.g., max 2 devices per license
* **Token revocation**: Expire access if user cancels payment
* **Tamper-proof local token**: Sign it with a private key on server

---

## **E. Tools to Help You**

* **Stripe Billing** – handles subscriptions & webhooks
* **Firebase Auth + Firestore** – fast auth + data store
* **Supabase** – Postgres + Auth, simple and open-source
* **Keygen.sh** – hosted license solution that supports account linking
* **JWT libraries** – for license tokens (available in all major languages)

---

## **F. Optional Enhancements**

* **Admin dashboard** to manage licenses manually
* **In-app upgrade**: Allow plan change from local UI
* **Webhook alerts** on suspicious activity (e.g., 5 devices per day)

---

## **Would You Like Help With:**

* Sample code for `license/check`?
* Machine ID generation (macOS, Windows, Linux)?
* Stripe webhook setup for license sync?

Just tell me your stack or language (Node, Python, etc.), and I can build the pieces for you.

---
